كتاب الإجارة في بيان أحكام هي بيع منفعة معلومة بأجر معلوم، وما صح ثمنا أي الإجارة كتاب الإجارة: لما اشتركت الهبة والإجارة في معنى التمليك، وكانت الهبة تمليك عين والإجارة تمليك منفعة، قدم تلك وأخر هذه؛ لكون العين أقوى، وهي في اللغة: اسم للأجرة [ أي كراء الأجير]، وهي ما يستحق على عمل الخير. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٢/٧] (فتح) هي بيع منفعة إلخ : يعني الإجارة شرعا تمليك منفعة بعوض، فخرج البيع والهبة والعارية والنكاح، فإنه استباحة المنافع بعوض، لا تمليكها، وأشار المصنف له إلى أن عقد الإجارة ينعقد بإقامة العين مقام المنفعة في حق الانعقاد، لا في حق الملك؛ لأن العقد لا بد له من محل؛ لأنه شرط للصحة لقول الفقهاء المحال شروط، ومحل العقد هنا المنافع وهي معدومة؛ والمعدوم لا يصلح محلا، فجعلت الدار محلا بإقامتها مقام المنافع، ولهذا لو أضاف العقد إلى المنافع لا يجوز بأن قال: آجرتك منافع هذه الدار شهرا بكذا، وإنما يصح بإضافته إلى العين. والمراد من انعقاد العلة ساعة فساعة في كلام مشايخنا على حسب حدوث المنافع، وهو عمل العلة، ونفاذها في المحل ساعة فساعة لا ارتباط الإيجاب والقبول كل ساعة وإن كان ظاهر كلام مشايخنا يوهم ذلك، والحكم تأخر من زمان انعقاد العلة إلى حدوث المنافع ساعة فساعة؛ لأن الحكم قابل للتراخي كما في البيع بشرط الخيار، ثم عقد الإجارة على ما عرف في أصول الفقه علة اسما؛ لإضافة الحكم إليه، ومعنى؛ لكونه مؤثرا، لا حكما؛ لتراخي الحكم عنه، كذا في "غاية البيان". وهذا تبين أن تعريف المصنف أولى من تعريف القدوري بقوله: "عقد على المنافع بعوض"؛ لما علمت أنها عقد على العين، وإنما المملوك المنافع، والمراد من المنفعة المنفعة المقصودة من العين حتى لو استأجر ثيابا ليبسطها، ولا يقعد عليها ولا ينام أو دابة ليربطها في فنائه، ويظن الناس أنها له أو ليجعلها جنيبة بين يديه أو آنية يضعها في بيته يتجمل بها ولا يستعملها، أو دارا لا يسكنها لكن ليظن الناس أنها له ملكا، أو عبدا على أن لا يستخدمه، أو دراهم يضعها، فالإجارة في جميع ذلك فاسدة ولا أجرة له كذا في "الخلاصة" من الجنس الثالث في الدواب. البحر الرائق: ٤٣٣/٧]
Book of Ijarah: Regarding the explanation of rulings. It (ijarah) is a sale of a known usufruct for a known rent. Kanz al-Daqaiq: Since hibah (gift) and ijarah share the meaning of tamlik (transfer of ownership), and hibah is a transfer of ownership of a corpus while ijarah is a transfer of ownership of a usufruct, the former was presented and the latter delayed because the corpus is stronger. In language, ijarah is a noun for the rent (meaning the hire of a worker), and it is what is earned for good work. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 7:432] (Fath) 'It is a sale of a usufruct etc.': meaning ijarah, according to shari'ah, is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) of a usufruct in exchange for compensation. Thus excluded are sale, gift, loan ('ariyah), and marriage (nikah), because those are permissibility (istibahah) of usufructs for compensation, not ownership (tamlik). The author indicated that the ijarah contract is concluded by placing the corpus (ayn) in the position of the usufruct with respect to the contract's formation, not with respect to ownership. Because a contract must have a subject matter (mahall); it is a condition for validity according to the jurists' statement 'The conditions for validity include the subject matter.' The subject matter of the contract here is the usufructs, which are nonexistent. Nonexistence cannot serve as a subject matter. So the house is made a subject matter by placing it in the position of the usufructs. Hence, if one added the contract to the usufructs, it would not be valid, such as saying 'I lease to you the usufructs of this house for a month for such-and-such.' It is only valid by adding it to the corpus. The meaning of 'the cause (illah) being concluded moment by moment' in the speech of our scholars is according to the genesis of the usufructs. That is, the effect of the cause and its penetration in the subject matter moment by moment, not that the offer and acceptance are connected each moment, even though the apparent meaning of our scholars' speech may suggest that. And the ruling (hukm) is delayed from the time of the conclusion of the cause to the genesis of the usufructs moment by moment, because the ruling can be delayed, as in a sale with a condition of an option. Then the ijarah contract, as known in usul al-fiqh, is a cause (illah) in name—because the ruling is attributed to it—and in meaning—because it is an effective cause—not a ruling (hukm) because the ruling is delayed from it. Thus in 'Ghayat al-Bayan'. This shows that the author's definition is superior to the definition of al-Quduri, who said 'a contract on usufructs for compensation', because you have learned that it is a contract on the corpus, and only the usufruct is owned. The intended meaning of 'usufruct' is the intended benefit from the corpus. So if someone hires clothes to spread them out but does not sit or sleep on them, or an animal to tie it in his courtyard and people think it is his, or to make it a 'janibah' (led alongside) before him, or vessels to place in his house for adornment without using them, or a house not to live in but so people think he owns it, or a slave with the condition not to employ him, or dirhams to place them, then the ijarah in all that is invalid (fasidah) and he is not owed rent. Thus in 'al-Khulasah' from the third type regarding animals. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 7:433]
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a definition and legal analysis of the ijarah contract according to the Hanafi school. It opens with the author's definition: ijarah is a sale of a known usufruct for a known rent (بَيْعُ مَنْفَعَةٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ بِأَجْرٍ مَعْلُومٍ). The commentator then expands this, stating that ijarah is in reality a tamlik (transfer of ownership) of the usufruct for a consideration, distinguishing it from sale (tamlik of the corpus), hibah (gratuitous transfer of corpus), 'ariyah (gratuitous loan of usufruct), and nikah (which is istibahah permissibility of usufruct, not tamlik). The crucial point of Hanafi legal theory is that the contract of ijarah is concluded on the corpus (الْعَيْن), not directly on the usufruct, because usufructs are nonexistent at the time of contract and cannot serve as a valid subject matter. Thus the corpus acts as a legal placeholder for the usufructs as they arise moment by moment. This is why it is invalid to say 'I lease you the usufructs of this house' directly; one must say 'I lease you this house.' The commentator then delves into the concept of the 'illah (cause) of the contract: the contract is the cause, but its effect (the hukm of ownership of usufruct) is delayed moment by moment as the usufructs arise. This is analogous to a sale with a condition of option, where the transfer of ownership is delayed. The author's definition is preferred over that of al-Quduri (عَقْدٌ عَلَى الْمَنَافِعِ بِعِوَضٍ) because al-Quduri's definition implies the contract is on the usufructs, whereas the correct Hanafi position is that the contract is on the corpus and only the usufructs are owned. The passage then provides examples of invalid ijarah (fāsidah) where the intended benefit (الْمَنْفَعَةُ الْمَقْصُودَة) is not the usual benefit of the object, such as hiring clothes only to spread out and not use, or an animal only to tie and show off. In such cases, the ijarah is void (fāsidah) and no rent is owed, because the usufruct is not the one customarily intended from that object.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijārah): A contract that transfers ownership (tamlik) of a known usufruct for a known rent.
عين (ʿayn): The specific physical object that is the subject matter of the contract (e.g., the house, the animal).
منفعة (manfaʿah): The usufruct or benefit derived from an object, which is the true intended subject matter of the ijarah contract.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; a key concept differentiating ijarah from ibāḥah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require that an ijarah contract be concluded on the ʿayn (corpus) rather than directly on the manfaʿah (usufruct)?
A) Because the ʿayn is more valuable than the manfaʿah.
B) Because usufructs are nonexistent at the time of contract and cannot serve as a subject matter.
C) Because the lessor only owns the ʿayn and cannot transfer the manfaʿah.
D) Because the lessee prefers to rent the physical object.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of ijarah centers on the transfer of ownership of a usufruct, but the contract itself must be anchored to the physical corpus to satisfy the requirement of an existing subject matter.

Invalid Ijarah: When the Intended Usufruct Is Not Customary
Provides examples of invalid ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an ijarah contract is invalid (fasid) due to lack of a legitimate intended usufruct and apply the rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Ijarah is void if the intended usufruct is not the customary benefit of the object, even if the parties agree.

The previous lesson established that ijarah is a transfer of ownership of a usufruct. But what if the intended usufruct is not what the object is customarily used for? The passage provides several examples where the contract is invalid (fasid) and no rent is owed. This lesson examines those examples and extracts the underlying condition: the usufruct must be the intended benefit (المنفعة المقصودة) from the corpus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
From the text: 'والمراد من المنفعة المنفعة المقصودة من العين' — the intended meaning of usufruct is the intended benefit from the corpus. This implies that the usufruct must be the customary or intended use of the object.
This is a condition of validity: the usufruct must be ma'qul (reasonable and customary).
2
List the examples provided
The text lists seven cases: (1) hiring clothes to spread out but not sit/sleep, (2) animal to tie in courtyard for show, (3) animal for janibah (led alongside), (4) vessels for adornment without use, (5) house for appearance of ownership, (6) slave with condition not to employ, (7) dirhams to place. For each, identify what the intended usufruct is and why it is not the customary benefit.
All share a common feature: the usufruct is not the primary benefit (e.g., clothes for wearing, animal for riding/transport, house for dwelling).
3
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Imagine hiring a car to park it in a garage and never drive it. Is the ijarah valid? Following the principle, the intended usufruct (parking only) is not the customary benefit of a car (transportation). Therefore, the ijarah is fasid and no rent is owed.
This extends the analogy from the animal and house examples.

Key Terms
منفعة مقصودة (manfaʿah maqsūdah): The intended or customary benefit of an object; if the benefit is not the usual one, the ijarah is invalid.
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): An invalid ijarah due to a flaw in a condition, such as the intended usufruct not being customary.

Which of the following ijarah contracts is fasid (invalid) according to the examples in the passage?

For an ijarah contract to be valid, the intended usufruct must be the customary benefit of the object; otherwise, the contract is fasid and no rent is due.

Valid Rent in Ijarah: Principles and Disputes
Ruling on valid rent types and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle 'ma saha thamanan saha ujrah', apply conditions for different types of rent (currency, fungibles, 'urud), and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on specifying the place of delivery for heavy fungibles.

Core Idea
Any valid price in a sale is valid as rent; but not conversely, and fungibles require salam-like conditions.

This lesson unpacks a foundational rule in Hanafi ijarah: anything that can serve as a price (thaman) in a sale can serve as rent (ujrah) in an ijarah contract. However, the types of rent vary in their requirements. We will explore the rules for currency, measurable/fungible goods, and non-fungible items like clothes, as well as a notable difference between Imam Abu Hanifah and his two disciples regarding the specification of the place of delivery for heavy fungible rents. Understanding these conditions is crucial for drafting valid ijarah contracts and avoiding disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Read the opening statement: 'ما صح ثمنا صح أجرة' (whatever is valid as a price is valid as rent). Understand the analogy (qiyas) – rent is the price of usufruct, so it follows sale price rules. Note that the converse does not hold, as usufruct can be rent but not price.
The principle is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
2
Analyze rent types: currency and specific items (a'yan)
For dirhams/dinars, the default is the prevalent currency; if mixed, the contract is fasid unless a specific currency is named. For a physical item ('ayn), it is valid as rent just as it is valid as a substitute in barter.
No term (ajal) is needed for 'ayn rent because it is delivered immediately.
3
Examine conditions for fungible rent (kili, wazni, adadi)
If the rent is a measurable, weighable, or countable fungible, you must specify the amount (qadr) and quality (sifah). Additionally, note the dispute: Abu Hanifah requires specifying the place of delivery if the item has transport cost (haml wa mu'nah); the Sahibayn do not require it at all.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (thamarah: fasid vs sahih if place unspecified).
4
Apply rules for 'urud (clothes and other goods)
For items categorized as 'urud (non-fungible goods), you must specify quantity, quality, and term (ajal). This is because a debt in the dhimmah can only be established through salam, so the conditions of salam apply.
The term is necessary for salam, hence required here.
5
Review the converse and exceptions
Understand that 'ma saha thamanan saha ujrah' does not imply the reverse. A usufruct (manfa'ah) cannot be a price but can be rent, provided the types are different (e.g., rent house for cultivating land). If types are same, it is invalid.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding.

وما صح أي ما جاز أن يكون ثمنا في البيع جاز أن يكون أجرة في الإجارة؛ لأن الأجرة ثمن المنفعة، فتعتبر بثمن المبيع، ومراده من الثمن ما كان بدلا عن شيء، فدخل فيه الأعيان، فإن العين تصلح بدلا في المقايضة، فتصلح أجرة، وأشار المصنف إلى أنها لو كانت الأجرة دراهم أو دنانير انصرفت إلى غالب نقد البلد، فإن كانت الغلبة مختلفة فالإجارة فاسدة ما لم يبين نقدا منها، فإن بين جاز، فإنها لو كانت كيليا أو وزنيا أو عدديا متقاربا، فالشرط فيه بيان القدر والصفة، ويحتاج فيه إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء إذا كان له حمل ومؤونة عند أبي حنيفة، وإن لم يكن له حمل ومؤونة، فلا يحتاج إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء، وعندهما ليس بشرط ولا يحتاج إلى بيان الأجل، فإن بين جاز وثبت، – وانها لو كانت ثيابا أو عروضا فالشرط فيه بيان القدر والأجل والصفة؛ لأنه لا يثبت دينا في الذمة إلا من جهة السلم، فكان لثبوته أصل واحد وهو السلم فلا يجوز إلا على شرائط السلم. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٣/٧] صح أجرة إلخ: أي كل شيء صح ثمنا في البيع صح أجرة في الإجارة، فإن كانت الأجرة عينا جاز كل عين أن يكون أجرة كما جاز أن يكون بدلا في البيع، وإن كان موصوفا في الذمة يجوز أيضا كل ما جاز أن يكون ثمنا أو مبيعا في الذمة كالمقدرات والمذروعات وما لا فلا وقوله: "ما صح ثمنا صح "أجرة" لا ينافي العكس، حتى صح أجرة ما لا يصح ثمنا كالمنفعة، فإنها لا تصلح ثمنا وتصلح أجرة إذا كانت مختلفة الجنس كاستئجار سكنى الدار بزراعة الأرض، وإن اتحد جنسهما لا يجوز كاستئجار الدار بسكنى الدار ، وكاستئجار الأرض للزراعة بزراعة أرض أخرى [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٨/٢]
And what is valid [as rent] means: whatever may be a price (thaman) in a sale may be rent (ujrah) in ijarah, because rent is the price of the usufruct, so it is considered analogously to the price of the sold item. By 'price' he means anything that serves as a substitute for something, so it includes physical items (a'yan), because a physical item can serve as a substitute in barter (muqayadah), so it can serve as rent. And the author indicated that if the rent is dirhams or dinars, it is referred to the predominant currency of the country. If the prevalence is mixed, the ijarah is invalid (fasidah) unless he specifies one of them; if he specifies, it is valid. If it is a measurable (kiliy), weighable (wazni), or countable (adadi mutaqarib) item, then it is necessary to specify the amount (qadr) and the quality (sifah). And according to Abu Hanifah, it is necessary to specify the place of delivery (makan al-ifa') if the item has transport cost and trouble (haml wa mu'nah); if not, then specifying the place of delivery is not necessary. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not a condition (shart) and it is not necessary to specify the term (ajal). If he specifies, it is valid and established. And if the rent is clothes or other goods, then it is necessary to specify the quantity, the term, and the quality, because a debt does not become established in the dhimmah (liability) except through salam. Thus its establishment has only one origin, which is salam, so it is not valid except according to the conditions of salam. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 7:433] 'Sa'a ujrah etc.': That is, everything that is valid as a price in a sale is valid as rent in ijarah. If the rent is a specific physical item ('ayn), then every 'ayn is valid as rent just as it is valid as a substitute in a sale. If it is described in the dhimmah (dayn), then everything that is valid as a price or sold item in the dhimmah is also valid, such as measured (muqaddarat) and weighed (madhrū'āt) items, and what is not [valid] is not [valid as rent]. His statement 'What is valid as price is valid as rent' does not negate the converse, so what is not valid as price may be valid as rent, such as a usufruct (manfa'ah): it is not valid as price but is valid as rent if the types are different, e.g., renting a house for residence in exchange for cultivating land. If the types are the same, it is not valid, such as renting a house for residence in exchange for residence in another house, or renting land for cultivation in exchange for cultivating another land. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:268]
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on what can serve as rent (ujrah) in an ijarah contract. The basic principle: anything that can be a valid price (thaman) in a sale can be a valid rent in ijarah, because rent is the price of the usufruct. This includes both specific physical items ('ayn) and debts (dayn) described in the dhimmah. For a rent that is dirhams or dinars, the default is the prevalent currency; if the prevalent currencies differ, the contract becomes fasid (invalid) unless the rent is specified. For fungible items (measurable, weighable, countable), the amount and quality must be specified. Additionally, according to Imam Abu Hanifah, if the rent consists of heavy items with transport cost, the place of delivery must be specified; otherwise, it is not required. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they consider place of delivery not a condition at all. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (difference within the school). The relied-upon fatwa position is not specified here. For rent that is non-fungible like clothes or other goods (categorized as 'urud), stricter conditions apply: quantity, term, and quality must be specified because such a rent becomes a debt in the dhimmah, which can only be established through the contract of salam (forward sale). So the conditions of salam apply. The commentator also clarifies the converse: the principle does not work both ways—something invalid as price can be valid as rent, such as a usufruct (manfa'ah). For example, renting a house in exchange for cultivating land is valid because the types differ (dwelling vs. agricultural benefit). But if the types are the same, it is invalid, like renting a house for another house's dwelling.

Key Terms
الأجرة (al-ujrah): The rent or consideration in an ijarah contract. It can be any valid price in a sale, including specific items or debts described in the dhimmah.
الكيلي (al-kaylī): A commodity measured by volume, e.g., grain, which if used as rent requires specification of quantity and quality.
السلم (al-salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later. Used as the exclusive basis for establishing a debt in the dhimmah.
العروض (al-ʿurūḍ): Non-fungible goods such as clothes, which when used as rent require full salam conditions (quantity, quality, term).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the rent consists of heavy goods (with transport cost), what is required according to Abu Hanifah?
A) Specification of the rent's quality only
B) Specification of the place of delivery
C) Specification of the term (ajal) only
D) No additional condition beyond quantity and quality

Key Takeaway
Valid rent in ijarah must meet conditions analogous to sale price, with additional specifics for fungibles and 'urud, and an intra-Hanafi dispute cautions specifying the place of delivery for heavy items.

Duration of Ijarah and Waqf Leases
Ruling on duration in ijarah and waqf leases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum duration of ijarah and waqf leases, explain the fatwa limit for waqf and its underlying rationale, and apply the legal stratagem (hilah) to extend the lease.

Core Idea
Ordinary ijarah has no maximum duration; for waqf, fatwa limits to three years to prevent ownership claims.

The usufruct (manfa‘ah) in a lease is legally known through its duration. In Hanafi fiqh, any clearly specified term makes the contract valid. However, a special protective rule applies to waqf (endowment) leases: the term must not exceed three years for agricultural land and one year for other properties, unless a greater benefit requires otherwise. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the Shafi‘i disagreement, and the legal strategies to extend the lease while staying within the law.

Guided Path
1
Identify how usufruct is known
The text states that usufruct is known through three matters; the first is specifying the duration. Focus on the rule that any duration, long or short, makes the usufruct known and the contract valid.
2
State the general ijarah ruling
The Hanafi position: any specified duration is valid—no maximum limit. Note the Shafi‘i objection (max one or three years) as a contrasting view.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Shafi‘i, a longer lease is invalid; in Hanafi, it is valid.
3
Apply the special waqf rule
For waqf properties, the fatwa restricts the term to three years (agricultural) or one year (non-agricultural) to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership. Understand the rationale: ‘khawf al-da‘wa’ (fear of claim).
This is a protective measure, not a strict legal requirement.
4
Examine the legal stratagems (hiyal)
The text mentions two hiyal: (1) contract separate one-year leases and document them as consecutive; (2) refer to the judge for authorization. Learn how these achieve a longer term without violating the rule.
The founder's stipulation overrides all; if he sets a term, it must be followed exactly.

والمنفعة تعلم إلخ أي المنفعة تعلم بأمور ثلاثة الأول ببيان المدة طالت أو قصرت كالسكنى والزراعة أي كمن استأجر دارا للسكنى وأرضا للزراعة، فيصح العقد على مدة معلومة أي مدة كانت، إلا في قول للشافعي لا تصح أكثر من سنة، وعنه أكثر ثلاث سنين، ويفتى في الوقف بثلاث سنين على ما أشار إليه بقوله: من "و لم تزد" إلخ. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٨/٢] أي مدة: بالجر بدل من مدة و"كان" حينئذ تامة، وبالنصب خبر مقدر لـ"كانت". (محشي) في الأوقاف إلخ: أي لم يزد في إجارة الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين خوفا من دعوى المستأجر الملكية عند تطاول المدة، والحيلة في الزيادة: أن يعقد عقودا كل عقد على سنة، ويكتب في الكتاب: أن فلان فلان استأجر الوقف بن وكذا سنة بكذا وكذا عقدا في كل سنة، وذكر صدر الإسلام له: أن الحيلة فيه أن يرفع إلى الحاكم حتى يجيزه، هذا إذا لم ينص الواقف على المدة، فإن نص على شيء يتبع ذلك طال أو قصر ؛ لأن نص الواقف كنص الشارع. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٨/٢] كذا على ثلاث سنين إلخ أطلقه فشمل الضياع ،وغيرها، وقد أفتى الصدر الشهيد بعدم الزيادة على ثلاث سنين في الضياع، وعلى سنة في غيرها، إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في غيره، قال في "المحيط": وهو المختار للفتوى. البحر الرائق: ٤٣٥/٧] وهذا عند عدم شرط الواقف فإن نص على شيء وزاد عليه لم يجز، وتفسخ في كل المدة على الراجح، إلا إذا كانت الزيادة على ما عينه الواقف أنفع، فيؤجره القاضي لا المتولي؛ لأن ولايته عامة. واعلم أن إجارة الوقف لا تصح إلا بأجرة المثل أو أكثر، فلو آجر الناظر بأقل لم يصح، ويلزم المستأجر تمام أجر المثل كذا في "البحر" و"الدر". (فتح)
And the usufruct is known etc.: meaning the usufruct is known through three matters: the first by specifying the duration, whether long or short, such as residence and cultivation—i.e., like someone who rents a house for residence or land for cultivation. So the contract is valid for a specified duration, whichever duration it may be. Except that according to al-Shafi‘i, it is not valid for more than one year, and there is a report from him that it is not valid for more than three years. And in the case of waqf (endowment), a fatwa is given for three years, as indicated by his statement 'and it is not increased' etc. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:268] 'Ay mudda': in the genitive as a substitute for 'mudda', and 'kan' then is complete; in the accusative it is a predicate implied for 'kanat'. (Hashiyah) 'In awqaf etc.': meaning it should not be increased in the ijarah of waqf properties beyond three years, for fear that the lessee might claim ownership if the term is prolonged. The legal stratagem (hilah) for extending it is to contract separate leases, each for one year, and write in the document: 'So-and-so leased the waqf property for such-and-such years at such-and-such rent, contract upon contract each year.' Sadr al-Islam mentioned a stratagem: to refer the matter to the judge so that he may authorize it. This applies if the founder did not specify the duration. If he specified something, it is followed, whether long or short, because the founder's stipulation is like the stipulation of the Lawgiver. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:268] Similarly, 'Three years etc.' He mentioned it absolutely, so it includes agricultural land (diya') and others. Sadr al-Shahid gave a fatwa against increasing beyond three years for agricultural lands, and one year for other properties, unless the benefit lies elsewhere. He said in 'al-Muhit': 'This is the chosen position for fatwa.' [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 7:435] This applies when the founder has not stipulated. If he stipulated something and [the lessor] increases beyond it, it is not permissible, and the contract is rescinded for the entire term according to the more correct view, unless the increase beyond what the founder specified is more beneficial. In that case, the judge (qadi) may lease it, not the trustee (mutawalli), because the judge's authority is general. Know that the ijarah of waqf is not valid except at the market rate (ujrat al-mithl) or more. So if the administrator (nazir) leases it for less, it is not valid, and the lessee is obliged to pay the full market rent. Thus in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Durr'. (Fath)
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage discusses how the usufruct (manfa‘ah) in an ijarah contract is legally known. The first method is by specifying the duration (muddah) of the lease. Any clear duration, long or short, is valid. The commentary notes a conflicting view from Imam al-Shafi‘i, who restricts the maximum term to one or three years. In the Hanafi school, however, there is no maximum term in principle. But for waqf (endowment) properties, a special ruling applies: the lease should not exceed three years, as per the fatwa. This is to prevent the lessee from wrongfully claiming ownership after a long possession. The text provides legal stratagems (hiyal) to extend the lease beyond three years, such as contracting separate one-year leases or referring to a judge. Importantly, if the founder of the waqf specified a duration, that must be followed absolutely, as the founder's stipulation is akin to the Lawgiver's text. Later Hanafi authorities refined the ruling: for agricultural lands (diya‘), the maximum is three years; for other properties, one year, unless the benefit requires otherwise. This is the relied-upon position (al-muhtar lil-fatwa). The passage also clarifies that the lease of waqf property must be at market rent (ujrat al-mithl) or more; any lease for less is invalid, and the lessee must pay the full market rate.

Key Terms
الوقف (al-waqf): An endowment of property for charitable purposes, where the corpus is permanently retained and the usufruct is directed to beneficiaries. Here, the rules of leasing waqf property are discussed.
أجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market rent for the property, which is the minimum acceptable rent for a waqf lease to be valid.
الحيلة (al-ḥīlah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible objective while staying within the bounds of the law. Here, it refers to ways to extend a waqf lease beyond three years without violating the rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (muhtar lil-fatwa) maximum term for leasing agricultural waqf lands according to the later Hanafi authorities?
A) One year
B) Three years
C) No limit
D) Ten years

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ijarah duration is unrestricted unless for waqf, where the fatwa limits it to three years (or one for non-agricultural) to protect endowment, though legal stratagems can extend the lease.

Rulings on Ujrah and Ownership in Ijarah
Ruling with proof: conditions of ujrah, specification of manfa'ah, and ownership of ujrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for specifying manfa'ah in an ijarah contract and explain the Hanafi ruling that ujrah is not owned by contract but by one of four events.

Core Idea
Ujrah is owned not at contract, but only when the benefit is enjoyed or payment is expedited.

In the Hanafi school, ijarah is a contract for exchanging benefit for payment. This lesson examines two essential aspects: what can serve as ujrah (consideration) and how the benefit must be specified so the contract is valid. Then we explore the Hanafi position on when the lessor actually owns the ujrah—a point of disagreement with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of a valid ijarah: ujrah and manfa'ah
Recognize that ujrah is the consideration and manfa'ah is the benefit, both must be known to avoid gharar.
The passage begins by stating what can be ujrah.
2
Understand the rule for ujrah: anything valid as a price is valid as ujrah, and benefit can be ujrah if types differ
The text states that whatever is valid as a price (thaman) in sale is valid as ujrah. Additionally, a benefit (manfa'ah) can be ujrah if the types of benefit differ.
This is a key Hanafi principle: benefit is not a valid price but can be ujrah.
3
Learn the three methods to specify manfa'ah: duration, specification (tasmia), pointing (ishara)
To avoid uncertainty, the benefit must be specified by one of these three methods. The passage provides examples: renting for a fixed period, hiring for a specific task, or transporting a specific item to a place.
Duration is the primary method; tasmia is for services; ishara is for identifying the subject matter.
4
Analyze the ownership of ujrah: not by contract, but by one of four events
The Hanafi school holds that ujrah is not owned immediately upon contract. Ownership occurs only when (1) the lessee expedites payment, (2) they condition expediting, (3) they enjoy the benefit, or (4) they are able to enjoy (tamakkun).
This is the central ruling of the passage and differs from other schools.
5
Examine the Hanafi proof and the inter-madhhab dispute
The Hanafi evidence is qiyas: since benefit is non-existent at contract, the countervalue cannot be owned immediately. Shafi'i and Ahmad argue ownership at contract; Malik says only by enjoyment.
The thamarah al-khilaf is when the lessor can demand payment.

Source Text

كتاب الإجارة
أحكام الإجارة
صح أجرة، والمنفعة تعلم ببيان المدة كالسكنى والزراعة، فتصح على مدة معلومة بأمور ثلاثة الأول أي مدة الاستئجار الإجارة أي مدة كانت، و لم تزد في الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين، طالت أو قصرت أي المدة = وأنها لو كانت ثيابا أو عروضا فالشرط فيه بيان القدر والأجل والصفة؛ لأنه لا يثبت دينا في الذمة إلا من جهة السلم، فكان لثبوته أصل واحد وهو السلم فلا يجوز إلا على شرائط السلم. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٣/٧] صح أجرة إلخ: أي كل شيء صح ثمنا في البيع صح أجرة في الإجارة، فإن كانت الأجرة عينا جاز كل عين أن يكون أجرة كما جاز أن يكون بدلا في البيع، وإن كان موصوفا في الذمة يجوز أيضا كل ما جاز أن يكون ثمنا أو مبيعا في الذمة كالمقدرات والمذروعات وما لا فلا وقوله: "ما صح ثمنا صح "أجرة" لا ينافي العكس، حتى صح أجرة ما لا يصح ثمنا كالمنفعة، فإنها لا تصلح ثمنا وتصلح أجرة إذا كانت مختلفة الجنس كاستئجار سكنى الدار بزراعة الأرض، وإن اتحد جنسهما لا يجوز كاستئجار الدار بسكنى الدار ، وكاستئجار الأرض للزراعة بزراعة أرض أخرى [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٨/٢] والمنفعة تعلم إلخ أي المنفعة تعلم بأمور ثلاثة الأول ببيان المدة طالت أو قصرت كالسكنى والزراعة أي كمن استأجر دارا للسكنى وأرضا للزراعة، فيصح العقد على مدة معلومة أي مدة كانت، إلا في قول للشافعي لا تصح أكثر من سنة، وعنه أكثر ثلاث سنين، ويفتى في الوقف بثلاث سنين على ما أشار إليه بقوله: من "و لم تزد" إلخ. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٨/٢] أي مدة: بالجر بدل من مدة و"كان" حينئذ تامة، وبالنصب خبر مقدر لـ"كانت". (محشي) في الأوقاف إلخ: أي لم يزد في إجارة الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين خوفا من دعوى المستأجر الملكية عند تطاول المدة، والحيلة في الزيادة: أن يعقد عقودا كل عقد على سنة، ويكتب في الكتاب: أن فلان فلان استأجر الوقف بن وكذا سنة بكذا وكذا عقدا في كل سنة، وذكر صدر الإسلام له: أن الحيلة فيه أن يرفع إلى الحاكم حتى يجيزه، هذا إذا لم ينص الواقف على المدة، فإن نص على شيء يتبع ذلك طال أو قصر ؛ لأن نص الواقف كنص الشارع. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٨/٢] كذا على ثلاث سنين إلخ أطلقه فشمل الضياع ،وغيرها، وقد أفتى الصدر الشهيد بعدم الزيادة على ثلاث سنين في الضياع، وعلى سنة في غيرها، إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في غيره، قال في "المحيط": وهو المختار للفتوى. البحر الرائق: ٤٣٥/٧] وهذا عند عدم شرط الواقف فإن نص على شيء وزاد عليه لم يجز، وتفسخ في كل المدة على الراجح، إلا إذا كانت الزيادة على ما عينه الواقف أنفع، فيؤجره القاضي لا المتولي؛ لأن ولايته عامة. واعلم أن إجارة الوقف لا تصح إلا بأجرة المثل أو أكثر، فلو آجر الناظر بأقل لم يصح، ويلزم المستأجر تمام أجر المثل كذا في "البحر" و"الدر". (فتح) أو بالتسمية كالاستئجار على صبغ الثوب وخياطته، أو بالإشارة كالاستئجار على نقل هذا الطعام إلى كذا والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد بل بالتعجيل موضع معلوم أي بنفس العقد أو بالتسمية إلخ [عطف على قوله ببيان المدة أي الثاني من الأمور الثلاث] أي يعلم المنفعة بالتسمية، وهو الأمر الثاني كالاستئجار على صبغ الثوب "و "خياطته" أي خياطة الثوب، وكذا استئجار الدابة للحمل عليها مقدارا ،معلوما، أو للركوب مسافة معلومة؛ لأنه إذا بين الثوب ولون الصبغ وقدره، وجنس الخياطة، وقدر المحمول وجنسه والمسافة صارت المنفعة معلومة بالتسمية [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٩/٢] أو بالإشارة إلخ : أي تعلم المنفعة بالإشارة، وهو الأمر الثالث كالاستئجار على نقل هذا الطعام إلى كذا أي إلى موضع عينه؛ لأنه إذا عيّن له المحمول وغاية الحمل تعينت المنفعة، فيصح العقد. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٩/٢] والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد: [سواء كانت الأجرة عينا أو دينا. (عيني)] أي لأن العقد ينعقد شيئا فشيئا على حسب حدوث المنفعة على ما بينا والعقد معاوضة، ومن قضيتها المساواة فمن ضرورة التراخي في جانب المنفعة التراخي في جانب البدل الآخر، فلا يعتق قريب المؤجر لو كان أجرة ولا يملك المطالبة بتسليمها للحال، ولا يلزم علينا صحة الإبراء عن الأجرة والكفالة والرهن بها؛ لأنا نقول ذلك بناء على وجود السبب، فصار كالعفو عن القصاص بعد وجود الجرح، كذا في غاية البيان"، لكن في "المحيط" أن جواز الإبراء قول محمد خلافا لأبي يوسف، وأشار المصنف إلى أنهما لو تصارفا بالأجرة، فأخذ بالدراهم ، دنانير لا يجوز، وهو قول أبي يوسف خلافا لمحمد، وإن كانت الأجرة نقرة بعينها لا تجوز المصارفة بها بالإجماع، والإبراء عن بعض الأجرة صحيح اتفاقا؛ لأنه بمنزلة الحط، كذا ذكره الولوالجي. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٦/٧] بل بالتعجيل إلخ أي بل تملك بأحد أربعة أشياء: الأول : بالتعجيل أي تعجيل المستأجر الأجرة، أو بشرطه أي أو بشرط التعجيل وهو الأمر الثاني، أو بالاستيفاء أي أو باستيفاء المعقود عليه وهي المنفعة، وهو الأمر الثالث، أو بالتمكن منه أي من الاستيفاء بتسليم العين المستأجرة في المدة، وهو الأمر الرابع، وقال الشافعي الله: تملك بنفس العقد، ويجب تسليمها عند تسليم العين المستأجرة؛ لأنها عقد معاوضة فيثبت الملك في البدلين بنفس و به قال أحمد لله، وقال مالك الله لا تملك إلا بالاستيفاء فقط، ولنا أن هذا عقد معاوضة، فيقتضي المساواة بينهما، وذلك بتقابل البدلين في الملك ،والتسليم وأحد البدلين وهو المنفعة لم تصر مملوكة بنفس العقد؛ لاستحالة ثبوت الملك في المعدوم، فكذا في البدل الآخر، ولو ملك الأجرة لملكها بغير بدل، وهو ليس من قضية المعاوضة، فيؤخر الملك فيه ضرورة إلى ما ذكرنا. العقد، فإن قلت: يصح الإبراء من اجرة بعد العقد، ولو لم يملكها لما صح، وكذا يصح الارتمان والكفالة بها، وكذا لو تزوج امرأة بسكنى داره سنة ويسلم الدار إليها ليس لها أن تمنع نفسها؟ قلت: لا يصح الإبراء عند أبي يوسف له .
Book of Ijarah. Rulings of Ijarah. Any [object] valid as a price is valid as ujrah. The benefit is known by specifying the duration, like renting a dwelling or agriculture. So [the contract] is valid for a specified period, by three matters: first, the period of hiring is any period, and it is not increased in endowments beyond three years, whether long or short. And if [the ujrah] were clothes or goods, the condition therein is specification of quantity, term, and description; because it is not established as a debt in the liability except through salam, so it has only one basis for establishment, which is salam, so it is not permissible except on the conditions of salam. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:433] 'صح أجرة etc.': i.e., anything valid as a price in sale is valid as ujrah in ijarah. If the ujrah is a specific object, every object is permissible as ujrah just as it is permissible as a substitute in sale. If it is described in the liability, it is also permissible whatever is permissible as a price or sold item in the liability, like measured and weighed items; otherwise not. His statement 'what is valid as a price is valid as ujrah' does not negate the converse, so it is valid as ujrah what is not valid as a price, like benefit, for benefit is not suitable as a price but is suitable as ujrah if the types differ, like renting a dwelling for cultivation of land; if their types are the same, it is not permissible, like renting a house for the dwelling of a house, or renting land for cultivation for cultivation of another land. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:268] 'The benefit is known etc.': i.e., the benefit is known by three matters: first, by specifying the duration, long or short, like dwelling and agriculture, e.g., one who rents a house for dwelling and land for agriculture; the contract is valid for a specified period, any period, except in one view of al-Shafi'i that it is not valid for more than one year, and from him more than three years; and fatwa is given in endowments for three years, as indicated by his saying 'and it is not increased' etc. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:268] 'any period': with jarr as a substitute for 'period', and 'was' here is complete; with nasb as an implied predicate of 'was'. (Margin note) 'In endowments etc.': i.e., it is not increased in the leasing of endowments beyond three years, fearing that the lessee might claim ownership if the period is long. The legal stratagem for increase is to make contracts, each contract for one year, and write in the document that so-and-so leased the endowment for such and such years with such and such a contract each year; and Sadr al-Islam mentioned that the stratagem is to raise it to the judge so that he may authorize it. This applies if the waqif did not specify the period; if he specified something, that is followed, long or short, because the specification of the waqif is like the specification of the Lawgiver. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:268] Similarly on three years etc.: he said it absolutely, so it includes lands and others. Sadr al-Shahid gave a fatwa that there is no increase beyond three years for lands, and beyond one year for others, unless the benefit lies in other than that; it is said in al-Muhit that this is the chosen [view] for fatwa. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:435] This is when the waqif did not specify a condition; if he specified something and it was exceeded, it is not permissible, and the contract is rescinded for the entire period according to the preferred view, unless the increase over what the waqif specified is more beneficial, then the judge leases it, not the trustee, because his jurisdiction is general. Know that leasing of endowment is not valid except for the market rate or more; if the overseer leases for less, it is not valid, and the lessee is compelled to pay the full market rate, as in al-Bahr and al-Durr. (Fatah) Or by specification, like hiring for dyeing a garment and tailoring it; or by pointing, like hiring for transporting this food to such and such. 'And the ujrah is not owned by the contract, but by expediting'... a known place... 'i.e., by the contract itself'... 'Or by specification etc.' [Apposition to his statement 'by specifying the period', i.e., the second of the three matters.] i.e., the benefit is known by specification, which is the second matter, like hiring for dyeing a garment and tailoring it, i.e., tailoring the garment; likewise, hiring an animal for carrying a known quantity, or for riding a known distance; because if he specifies the garment, the color of the dye and its quantity, the type of tailoring, the quantity of the load and its type, and the distance, the benefit becomes known by specification. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:269] 'Or by pointing etc.': i.e., the benefit is known by pointing, which is the third matter, like hiring for transporting this food to such and such, i.e., to a specific place; because if he specifies the load for him and the endpoint of transport, the benefit is determined, so the contract is valid. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:269] 'And the ujrah is not owned by the contract': [whether the ujrah is a specific object or a debt. (Ayni)] i.e., because the contract is formed little by little according to the occurrence of the benefit, as we have explained; and the contract is an exchange, and its requirement is equivalence, so from the necessity of delay in the benefit side is delay in the other countervalue side. Thus, the relative of the lessor is not freed if he is the ujrah, nor can he demand delivery of it immediately. This does not entail the validity of release from ujrah, suretyship, or pledge with it; for we say that [those] are based on the existence of a cause, so it becomes like pardon for qisas after injury occurs, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. However, in al-Muhit, the permissibility of release is the view of Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. The author indicated that if they engage in a currency exchange for the ujrah, taking drachmas for dinars, it is not permissible; this is the view of Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. If the ujrah is a specific silver nugget, currency exchange for it is not permissible by consensus. Release from part of the ujrah is valid by agreement because it is like a reduction. Thus mentioned by al-Walwaliji. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:436] 'Rather, by expediting etc.': i.e., it is owned by one of four things: first, by expediting, i.e., the lessee's expediting the ujrah; or by its condition, i.e., the condition of expediting, which is the second matter; or by enjoyment, i.e., by enjoying the contracted object, which is the benefit, and that is the third matter; or by ability to do so, i.e., to enjoy, by handing over the leased object during the period, which is the fourth matter. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: it is owned by the contract itself, and it must be delivered upon handing over the leased object, because it is an exchange contract, so ownership is established in both countervalues by the contract; and Ahmad, may Allah have mercy on him, said the same. Malik, may Allah have mercy on him, said: it is owned only by enjoyment alone. Our evidence: this is an exchange contract, so it requires equivalence between the two, and that is by mutual correspondence of the two countervalues in ownership and delivery. One of the countervalues, the benefit, does not become owned by the contract itself, because it is impossible to establish ownership of a non-existent thing; so likewise for the other countervalue. If he owned the ujrah, he would own it without a countervalue, which is not from the requirement of exchange; so ownership is delayed necessarily to what we have mentioned. The contract [is not enough]. If you say: release from ujrah after the contract is valid, and if he did not own it, it would not be valid; likewise, pledge and suretyship for it are valid; likewise, if a man marries a woman for the dwelling of his house for a year and hands over the house to her, does she not have the right to prevent herself? We say: release is not valid according to Abu Yusuf, for him.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof commentary from the Hanafi school on the basic rulings of ijarah (lease/hire contracts). It is an expansion probe of the matn, explaining the key principles regarding ujrah (consideration) and manfa'ah (benefit). The commentary begins by establishing that anything valid as a price in a sale (bay') is also valid as ujrah in ijarah. This includes both specific objects (ayn) and debts described in the liability (dayn). Importantly, the converse is not necessarily true: a manfa'ah (benefit) can serve as ujrah even though it cannot be a price, provided the types of benefit differ (e.g., renting a house for cultivation of land). If the benefits are of the same type, it is not permissible. The passage then explains the three ways to specify the manfa'ah so that the contract is valid: (1) specifying the duration (e.g., rental period), (2) specifying the task (tasmia, e.g., dyeing or tailoring a garment), and (3) pointing (ishara, e.g., transporting this specific food to a specific location). The text includes a detailed discussion on leasing of awqaf (endowments), where the default is a maximum of three years to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership. If the waqif specified a term, that must be followed. The commentary also addresses legal stratagems (hiyal) for extending beyond three years and the rule that the ujrah must be at the market rate or higher. The second major topic is the ownership of ujrah. The Hanafi position, as stated, is that ujrah is not owned by the contract itself. Instead, it becomes owned by one of four events: (a) the lessee expediting payment (ta'jil), (b) a contractual condition for immediate payment, (c) actual enjoyment of the benefit (istifa'), or (d) the ability to enjoy (tamakkun) after the leased object is made available. The commentary provides the reasoning: ijarah is an exchange where the benefit is realized gradually, so the countervalue cannot be owned immediately; otherwise, it would be an exchange without immediate countervalue. This rational argument (istihsan) counters the positions of Shafi'i and Ahmad, who hold that ujrah is owned at contract, and Malik, who holds it is owned only by enjoyment. The passage also addresses objections regarding the validity of release (ibra'), pledge (rahn), and suretyship (kafala) with respect to ujrah, noting an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that ibra' is valid (Muhammad's view). Overall, this passage establishes the fundamental framework of ijarah contracts in the Hanafi school, emphasizing the need for clarity in benefit and the deferred ownership of the countervalue.

Key Terms
أجرة (ujrah): Consideration in a lease/hire contract; it can be a specific object, a debt, or a benefit (if of a different type).
منفعة (manfa'ah): The benefit or utility derived from the leased object, which is the subject matter of the contract.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract for the hire/lease of services or use of property in exchange for ujrah.
تسمية (tasmia): Specification of the benefit by describing the task (e.g., dyeing, tailoring) or the quantity and type of load/distance.
إشارة (ishara): Pointing to the specific item or location to specify the benefit (e.g., transporting this food to that place).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the lessor own the ujrah (consideration) in a valid ijarah contract?
A) At the moment the contract is signed.
B) Only after the entire lease period ends.
C) By one of four events: expediting payment, its condition, enjoyment of benefit, or ability to enjoy.
D) Only upon actual physical delivery of the ujrah.

Key Takeaway
Ujrah is not owned by contract but by one of four events; benefit must be specified by duration, description, or pointing.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Specifying Benefit and the Deferred Ownership of Wage in Ijarah
Explains three ways to specify benefit and the deferred ownership of wage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three ways to specify the benefit in ijarah and apply the Hanafi principle that the wage is not owned by contract but by one of four events.

Core Idea
The wage is not owned by contract; it is owned only by acceleration, condition, usufruct, or ability to usufruct.

Ijarah is a contract exchanging a known benefit for a known wage. But when does the wage actually become owned? The Hanafi school answers with a precise principle: the wage is deferred to match the gradual emergence of the benefit. In this lesson, we will explore how the benefit must be specified—by duration, by naming, or by indication—and then examine the four events that trigger ownership of the wage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three methods of specifying benefit
The passage lists three ways the benefit (manfa'ah) can be made known in an ijarah contract: by specifying the duration (ta'yin al-mudda), by naming the task (tasmiah), or by indicating the object (isharah). Work through each method and the examples given.
The first method (time) is mentioned earlier; the passage expands on naming and indication.
2
State the Hanafi rule on wage ownership
The core rule: 'al-ujrah la tumlak bi al-aqd' (the wage is not owned by the contract). Understand that ownership is deferred because the benefit comes into existence gradually.
This is a rational (aqli) argument based on the nature of exchange and the impossibility of owning a non-existent thing.
3
List the four events that cause wage ownership
From the commentary: by acceleration (ta'jil), its condition (shart al-ta'jil), actual usufruct (istifa'), or ability to take usufruct (tamakkun). Know each definition.
Tamakkun occurs when the leased object is delivered and the lessee is able to use it, even if they don't actually use it.
4
Analyze the rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
The Hanafi argument: since benefit is non-existent at contract, immediate wage ownership would create imbalance. Ownership must parallel the gradual existence of the benefit.
This proof rebuts the Shafi'i position that wage is owned by contract itself.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad permits remission (ibra') of the wage after contract, while Abu Yusuf does not. Understand how this connects to the ownership debate.
This shows that even within the school, the implications of deferred ownership are nuanced.

موضع معلوم
أي بنفس العقد
أو بالتسمية إلخ [عطف على قوله ببيان المدة أي الثاني من الأمور الثلاث] أي يعلم المنفعة بالتسمية، وهو الأمر الثاني كالاستئجار على صبغ الثوب "و "خياطته" أي خياطة الثوب، وكذا استئجار الدابة للحمل عليها مقدارا ،معلوما، أو للركوب مسافة معلومة؛ لأنه إذا بين الثوب ولون الصبغ وقدره، وجنس الخياطة، وقدر المحمول وجنسه والمسافة صارت المنفعة معلومة بالتسمية [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٩/٢] أو بالإشارة إلخ : أي تعلم المنفعة بالإشارة، وهو الأمر الثالث كالاستئجار على نقل هذا الطعام إلى كذا أي إلى موضع عينه؛ لأنه إذا عيّن له المحمول وغاية الحمل تعينت المنفعة، فيصح العقد. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٦٩/٢] والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد: [سواء كانت الأجرة عينا أو دينا. (عيني)] أي لأن العقد ينعقد شيئا فشيئا على حسب حدوث المنفعة على ما بينا والعقد معاوضة، ومن قضيتها المساواة فمن ضرورة التراخي في جانب المنفعة التراخي في جانب البدل الآخر، فلا يعتق قريب المؤجر لو كان أجرة ولا يملك المطالبة بتسليمها للحال، ولا يلزم علينا صحة الإبراء عن الأجرة والكفالة والرهن بها؛ لأنا نقول ذلك بناء على وجود السبب، فصار كالعفو عن القصاص بعد وجود الجرح، كذا في غاية البيان"، لكن في "المحيط" أن جواز الإبراء قول محمد خلافا لأبي يوسف، وأشار المصنف إلى أنهما لو تصارفا بالأجرة، فأخذ بالدراهم دنانير لا يجوز، وهو قول أبي يوسف خلافا لمحمد، وإن كانت الأجرة نقرة بعينها لا تجوز المصارفة بها بالإجماع، والإبراء عن بعض الأجرة صحيح اتفاقا؛ لأنه بمنزلة الحط، كذا ذكره الولوالجي. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٦/٧]
بل بالتعجيل إلخ أي بل تملك بأحد أربعة أشياء: الأول : بالتعجيل أي تعجيل المستأجر الأجرة، أو بشرطه أي أو بشرط التعجيل وهو الأمر الثاني، أو بالاستيفاء أي أو باستيفاء المعقود عليه وهي المنفعة، وهو الأمر الثالث، أو بالتمكن منه أي من الاستيفاء بتسليم العين المستأجرة في المدة، وهو الأمر الرابع، وقال الشافعي الله: تملك بنفس العقد، ويجب تسليمها عند تسليم العين المستأجرة؛ لأنها عقد معاوضة فيثبت الملك في البدلين بنفس و به قال أحمد لله، وقال مالك الله لا تملك إلا بالاستيفاء فقط، ولنا أن هذا عقد معاوضة، فيقتضي المساواة بينهما، وذلك بتقابل البدلين في الملك والتسليم وأحد البدلين وهو المنفعة لم تصر مملوكة بنفس العقد؛ لاستحالة ثبوت الملك في المعدوم، فكذا في البدل الآخر، ولو ملك الأجرة لملكها بغير بدل، وهو ليس من قضية المعاوضة، فيؤخر الملك فيه ضرورة إلى ما ذكرنا.
العقد،
فإن قلت: يصح الإبراء من اجرة بعد العقد، ولو لم يملكها لما صح، وكذا يصح الارتمان والكفالة بها، وكذا لو تزوج امرأة بسكنى داره سنة ويسلم الدار إليها ليس لها أن تمنع نفسها؟ قلت: لا يصح الإبراء عند أبي يوسف [؟]
Book of Ijarah: Rulings of Ijarah: Or by naming, like hiring for dyeing a garment and sewing it; or by indication, like hiring for transporting this food to such-and-such place. The wage is not owned by the contract but by acceleration... Meaning: by the contract itself. 'Or by naming etc.' is an attachment to his statement 'by specifying the duration' i.e. the second of the three matters. That is, the benefit is known by naming, which is the second matter, like hiring for dyeing the garment and sewing it, i.e. sewing the garment. Similarly, hiring an animal to carry a known quantity or to ride a known distance, because if he specifies the garment, the color of the dye, its quantity, the type of sewing, the quantity and type of the load, and the distance, the benefit becomes known by naming. Or by indication etc.: i.e., the benefit is known by indication, which is the third matter, like hiring for transporting this food to such-and-such a specific place, because if he specifies the load and the destination, the benefit is determined, so the contract is valid. And the wage is not owned by the contract: (whether the wage is a specific object or a debt). That is, because the contract comes into existence gradually according to the occurrence of the benefit, as we have explained. The contract is an exchange, and its requirement is equality. So from the necessity of delay on the side of the benefit, there is delay on the side of the other consideration. Thus, the relative of the lessor is not freed if he is the wage, nor does he have the right to demand its delivery immediately. The validity of remitting the wage, guaranteeing it, and pawning it does not contradict us, because we say that is based on the existence of the cause, so it becomes like pardoning retaliation after the infliction of injury. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. But in al-Muhit, the permissibility of remission is the saying of Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. The author indicated that if they exchange the wage, taking dinars for dirhams, it is not permissible – that is Abu Yusuf's saying, contrary to Muhammad. If the wage is a specific silver nugget, exchanging it is not permissible by consensus. Remitting part of the wage is valid by agreement, because it is like a reduction. Thus mentioned by al-Walwaliji. But by acceleration etc.: i.e., it is owned by one of four things: first, by acceleration: i.e., the lessee accelerating the wage; or by its condition: i.e., the condition of acceleration, which is the second matter; or by usufruct: i.e., by taking the subject matter of the contract, which is the benefit, and that is the third matter; or by being able to do so: i.e., by being able to take usufruct through delivery of the leased object within the period, and that is the fourth matter. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is owned by the contract itself, and it must be delivered upon delivery of the leased object, because it is an exchange contract, so ownership of both considerations is established by the contract itself. Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on him) said the same. Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is only owned by usufruct alone. Our evidence: This is an exchange contract, so it requires equality between them, which is by the matching of the two considerations in ownership and delivery. One of the two considerations, the benefit, is not owned by the contract itself because it is impossible to establish ownership of something non-existent, so likewise the other consideration. If the wage were owned, it would be owned without a countervalue, which is not a requirement of exchange. So ownership is necessarily delayed to what we have mentioned. The contract: If you say: Remission of the wage after the contract is valid, and if it were not owned it would not be valid. Similarly, pawning and guaranteeing it are valid. Similarly, if a man marries a woman with the right to live in his house for a year and he delivers the house to her, she should not prevent herself? I say: Remission is not valid according to Abu Yusuf [?]
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary explains the foundational rulings of ijarah. The text begins by stating three ways the benefit (manfa'ah) in a hire contract can be specified: by naming (tasmiah), like hiring for a specific dyeing job; by indication (isharah), like transporting this specific food; and by specifying duration (mentioned earlier). The wage (ujrah) is not owned by the contract itself but by one of four events: acceleration (ta'jil) of payment, a condition for acceleration, actual usufruct (istifa'), or ability to take usufruct (tamakkun). The commentator clarifies that the reason wage is not owned by contract is that the benefit comes into existence gradually; ownership of the wage must parallel this. The Hanafi school uses rational argument (qiyas) to rebut Imams al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, who hold that wage is owned by contract, and Imam Malik, who holds ownership only by actual usufruct. The Hanafi position is that immediate ownership of wage would mean owning it without a countervalue, since the benefit is not yet fully realizable. The commentary also addresses subsidiary issues: remission (ibra') of wage is valid according to Imam Muhammad but not Abu Yusuf; exchange (sarf) of wage is governed by specific rules. This lesson covers the core principle that wage ownership is deferred commensurate with the benefit.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract to exchange a known benefit (manfa'ah) for a known compensation (ujrah).
المنفعة (al-manfa'ah): The benefit that is the subject matter of the ijarah contract; it comes into existence over time.
الأجرة (al-ujrah): The wage or rental payment given in exchange for the benefit.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Acceleration of payment; one of the four ways the wage becomes owned.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Actual taking of the benefit (usufruct); another way the wage is owned.
الإشارة (al-isharah): Indication; a method of specifying the benefit by pointing to the specific object or task.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT one of the four events that cause ownership of the wage in ijarah?
A) Acceleration of payment (ta'jil)
B) Specifying the benefit by naming (tasmiah)
C) Usufruct (istifa')
D) Ability to take usufruct (tamakkun)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the wage in ijarah is not owned by contract; it becomes owned only by acceleration, its condition, actual usufruct, or the ability to take usufruct.

The Three Methods of Wage Ownership and the Effect of Usurpation in Ijarah
Details the three methods of wage ownership and rulings on usurpation and payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three methods of wage ownership in valid ijarah, explain why tamakkun suffices for wage obligation, and distinguish the two Hanafi views on whether usurpation dissolves the contract.

Core Idea
Wage is owed by tamakkun (ability) alone; usurpation dissolves the contract and drops the wage proportionally.

This lesson unpacks the three methods by which the wage (ujrah) becomes owned in a valid ijarah, including the critical concept of tamakkun. We'll examine the rule that possession and ability to use are sufficient for the wage to be due, even without actual use. The passage also addresses the controversial effect of usurpation by the lessor: does it dissolve the contract or merely suspend the wage? We'll explore the relied-upon view and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three methods of wage ownership
The passage mentions 'by its condition' (shart al-ta'jil), 'by usufruct' (al-isti'fa'), and 'by ability' (al-tamakkun). Note that the first method (possibly 'by contract') was covered in the prior lesson.
Focus on tamakkun as the main point here.
2
Apply the rule for tamakkun in valid vs fasid ijarah
In valid ijarah, possession/ability suffices for wage due even without actual use. In fasid (void) ijarah, only actual benefit triggers wage obligation, except for waqf properties where tamakkun suffices.
Waqf is an exception; see the commentary on al-Is'af.
3
Analyze the effect of usurpation (ghasb/hailulah) by the lessor
If the lessor prevents the lessee from using the object, the wage falls entirely (if whole period) or proportionally (if part). The text indicates that this implies dissolution of the contract, per al-Hidayah, contrary to Qadi Khan.
Usurpation here means prevention, not actual tort, since real estate cannot be truly usurped.
4
Examine default payment terms when not specified
For a house, the lessor may demand wage daily; for a camel hire, at each stage. If specified (e.g., after two months), the specified time governs.
This is because benefit accrues incrementally and payment is tied to realization.

[البحر الرائق: ٤٣٧/٧] قال في "الفتح": وثمرة الاختلاف في أن الغصب هل يوجب فسخ الإجارة أم لا؟ تظهر فيما إذا زال الغصب قبل قضاء المدة، فعلى القول بعدم الفسخ المدة، يستوفي ما بقي من وعليه من الأجر بحسابه.

Or by its condition, or by usufruct, or by being able to do so. If it is usurped from him, the wage falls. And for the owner of the house and land, he may demand the wage every day; and for the camel driver, every stage, the owner of the camel. = - Because it is not obligatory, unlike deferred debt, because it is established in the liability. As for the saying of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him): because the cause of its obligation exists, so remission is permissible after the existence of the cause, like remission of retaliation after injury. Pledge and guarantee are for security, so actual obligation is not required. Do you not see that they are both permissible for the price in a sale with a condition of option, and for a promised debt? Guarantee of liability (al-darak) is permissible, and it is permissible to suspend it on a condition. Similarly for this debt. The woman may not detain herself after the delivery of the house to her, because he has fulfilled what he named for her with her consent, and that is the intended meaning of such a custom when unrestricted. So it becomes as if she deferred the entire dowry; then she is obliged to surrender herself before it is due. Thus this, even more so, because she has taken possession of the house, and it stands in place of the benefit in some respects. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 269/2] Or by its condition: i.e., the condition of acceleration, and this applies to non-deferred ijarah. As for deferred ijarah, the condition of acceleration is invalid, and nothing is incumbent upon him immediately, because the non-obligation of the wage therein is not due to the contract's requirement, but due to the explicit deferment to a time that does not exist before that time. (Fath) Or by being able to do so: i.e., by being able to take the subject matter of the contract. If he takes possession of the house, the wage is due even if he does not reside. Similarly, if he hires an animal to ride to Mecca and takes it to Mecca but does not ride, the wage is due. This applies when the ijarah is valid. As for a void (fasid) ijarah, the wage is only due by actual benefit. What is apparent in al-Is'af excludes waqf; thus its void ijarah wage is due by ability (tamakkun). I say: Is the property of an orphan, property prepared for lease, and property leased in a sale with the right of repurchase (bay' al-wafa) similar, according to the fatwa of the scholars of Rum? It is a point of hesitation. Thus in al-Tanwir and its commentary. Then: If it is usurped from him, etc.: i.e., if the lessor usurps the leased object from the lessee, the wage falls, because the delivery of the place is only established as a substitute for the benefit for the ability to benefit. So if the ability is lost, the delivery is lost. His statement 'the wage falls' indicates that the contract is dissolved by usurpation, as stated in al-Hidayah, contrary to Qadi Khan. It is general, covering if the usurpation covers the entire period – then the entire wage falls – and if it covers part, then it falls proportionally. It includes real estate and other things. His intention of 'usurpation' here is prevention (hailulah) between the lessee and the object, not the actual usurpation (ghasb) because, in our school, usurpation does not apply to real estate. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 437/7] It is said in al-Fath: The practical difference regarding whether usurpation dissolves the contract or not appears in the case where the usurpation ends before the expiry of the period. According to the view that it does not dissolve, the lessee may take the remaining benefit, and the wage is due proportionally. Delivery: And for the owner of the house, etc.: because it is a desired benefit, and what is less than a day has no limit, so it becomes like maintenance (nafaqah) which can be demanded at evening every hour. He intended it when unrestricted. But if he specifies the time of payment in the contract, it is determined, because it is like acceleration, as if he said: 'I lease you this house for a year on condition that you give the wage after two months.' [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 438/7] And for the camel driver, etc.: i.e., the camel driver may demand the wage at every stage he completes, which is what the author expressed as 'the owner of the camel' – meaning that the camel driver (the owner of the camel) may demand the wage at every stage if the time of payment is not specified. If he specifies, saying 'on condition that I give the wage after two months,' he may demand it after that. (Miskin)

Commentary
This second lesson continues the commentary on the four ways the wage is owned, specifically focusing on the condition of acceleration (shart al-ta'jil) and ability (tamakkun). The text explains that if the lessee is able to take benefit (e.g., possession of the house is delivered), the wage is due even without actual use. This applies to valid ijarah; in fasid ijarah, wage is only due by actual benefit, except for waqf property where ability suffices. A key ruling: if the lessor usurps the object (or prevents the lessee from using it), the wage falls entirely or proportionally, and the contract is dissolved according to al-Hidayah, contra Qadi Khan. The text also addresses payment terms: if not specified, the lessor of a house can demand wage daily, and a camel driver can demand at each stage. These defaults apply because the benefit accrues incrementally. The commentary includes a discussion on whether ibra' (remission) is valid: it is permissible according to Imam Muhammad because the cause exists, even if the wage is not yet due. The example of a woman marrying for residency: after receiving the house, she cannot withhold herself, analogous to deferred dower. The lesson reinforces that wage ownership and payment are tied to the gradual realization of benefit.

Key Terms
التمكن (al-tamakkun): Ability to take usufruct of the leased object; one of the methods by which the wage is owned. Once the lessee has possession and is able to use it, the wage is due.
الغصب (al-ghasb): In this context, usurpation or prevention (hailulah) by the lessor that deprives the lessee of the ability to benefit.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Remission of a debt; the text discusses its validity for the wage after contract but before ownership.
الإجارة المضافة (al-ijarah al-mudafah): Deferred ijarah where the period starts at a future date. In such contracts, a condition of immediate acceleration is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In a valid ijarah contract, if the lessor prevents the lessee from using the property for a portion of the term, what is the ruling on the wage?
A) The full wage remains due
B) The wage falls only for the period of prevention
C) The contract is automatically extended
D) The lessee must pay half the wage

Key Takeaway
In valid ijarah, wage is due upon tamakkun; usurpation by the lessor dissolves the contract and drops the wage proportionally.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
advanced
8 min
Conditions for Wage Obligation in Ijarah and Effect of Usurpation
Ruling on causes for wage due and effect of usurpation in ijarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three ways wage becomes due in a valid ijarah, apply the rule of tamakkun, and explain the effect of ghasp on the contract and wage.

Core Idea
Wage is due by condition, use, or ability to use; usurpation voids the contract and drops the wage.

This lesson examines a key passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the circumstances that make the rental payment obligatory. The Hanafi school recognizes three triggers: a stipulation for immediate payment, actual use, or the ability to use without actual use. Additionally, if the hired object is taken from the lessee by the lessor or a third party, the contract dissolves and the wage is dropped for that period. The commentary expands on nuances such as deferred ijarah and invalid ijarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three triggers for wage
The matn lists 'bi-shartih, bi al-istifa', bi al-tamakkun'. Recognize that these are alternative conditions for wage obligation in a valid ijarah.
2
Understand tamakkun as sufficient
Tamakkun (ability to use) triggers wage even without actual use. This is unique to the Hanafi school; in fasid ijarah, actual use is required.
Example: taking possession of a house makes wage due even if not lived in.
3
Analyze the effect of ghasp
If the hired object is usurped (ghasp) from the lessee, the ability to use is lost, so the wage drops. According to the relied Hanafi view, the contract dissolves automatically.
This applies to both movable and immovable property (though land is not technically ghasp).
4
Recognize the intra-madhhab dispute
Qadikhan held that ghasp does not dissolve the contract; instead, it gives an option. The mufta bihi is dissolution, as preferred by Al-Hidayah.
The thamarah (practical consequence) appears when ghasp ends before the term: on dissolution, no further obligation; on non-dissolution, the lessee continues and pays proportionally.
5
Apply partial ghasp
If ghasp occurs for only part of the term, wage drops proportionally for that period.
Example: if usurped for 3 months of a 12-month lease, only 9 months' rent is due.

Source Text

(فتح) أو بالتمكن منه أي بالتمكن من استيفاء المعقود عليه بأن قبض الدار فعليه الأجرة، وإن لم يسكن، وكذا لو استأجر دابة ليركبها إلى مكة فذهب بها إلى مكة ولم يركب، تجب الأجرة، وهذا إذا كانت الإجارة صحيحة، أما في الفاسدة: فلا يجب الأجر إلا بحقيقة الانتفاع، وظاهر ما في "الإسعاف" إخراج الوقف، فتجب أجرته الفاسدة بالتمكن، قلت: وهل مال اليتيم والمعد للاستغلال والمستأجر في البيع وفاء على ما أفتى به علماء الروم كذلك؟ محل تردد، كذا في "التنوير" و"شرحه". فإن غصب منه إلخ أي فإن غصب المؤجر العين المستأجرة من المستأجر سقط الأجر؛ لأن تسليم المحل إنما أقيم مقام المنفعة للتمكن من الانتفاع، فإذا فات التمكن فات التسليم، وأشار بقوله: "سقط الأجر" إلى أن العقد ينفسخ بالغصب، كما صرح به في "الهداية"، خلافا لقاضي خان، وأطلقه، فشمل ما إذا غصب في جميع المدة، فيسقط جميع الأجر، وأما إذا غصب في بعضها فبحسابه، وشمل العقار وغيره، ومراده من الغصب هنا الحيلولة بين المستأجر والعين، لا حقيقة الغصب؛ إذ الغصب لا يجري في العقار عندنا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٧/٧] قال في "الفتح": وثمرة الاختلاف في أن الغصب هل يوجب فسخ الإجارة أم لا؟ تظهر فيما إذا زال الغصب قبل قضاء المدة، فعلى القول بعدم الفسخ المدة، يستوفي ما بقي من وعليه من الأجر بحسابه.
Or by its condition, or by actual use, or by ability to use. If he usurps it from him, the wage drops. ...
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on when the wage in an ijarah contract becomes due, and what happens if the hired object is usurped. The matn states three ways the wage becomes obligatory: (1) by stipulating immediate payment (bishart ta'jeel), (2) by actually using the hired object (bil-istifa'), or (3) by being able to use it even without actual use (bil-tamakkun). If the owner (or another) usurps the object from the lessee, the wage is dropped because the ability to use is lost. The commentary expands: the first scenario (by condition) is valid only in non-deferred ijarah; if the ijarah is future (mudhaf), stipulating immediate payment is void. The second scenario: if the lessee takes possession of the house, wage is due even without living in it, and similarly for a mount. The third scenario applies to valid ijarah; in invalid (fasid) ijarah, wage is only due by actual use. For usurpation (ghasp), the contract dissolves (yansakh) automatically according to Al-Hidayah, contrary to Qadikhan's view. If the usurpation ends before the term, on the view of non-dissolution, the lessee continues and pays proportionally.

Key Terms
الإستيفاء (al-istifa'): Actual receipt and use of the hired benefit by the lessee.
التمكن (al-tamakkun): The ability to use the hired object without actual use, e.g., taking possession of a house.
الغصب (al-ghasp): Unlawful seizure of property, here specifically preventing the lessee from using the hired object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a valid ijarah, which of the following triggers the wage even without actual use?
A) Only a stipulation for immediate payment.
B) Only actual use.
C) Tamakkun (ability to use).
D) No trigger; wage is always deferred.

Key Takeaway
Wage in ijarah is due by condition, actual use, or simply the ability to use; usurpation dissolves the contract and drops the wage for that period.

Timing of Wage in Ijarah: Default Payment Intervals
Ruling on default payment intervals for ijarah of property and transport

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default rule for when a lessor or transport provider may demand payment in an ijarah contract and identify the exception when a payment schedule is specified.

Core Idea
Rent is due daily, camel hire per stage — unless the contract fixes the payment time.

When an ijarah contract is silent on payment timing, Hanafi fiqh provides default rules to prevent dispute. This lesson presents those defaults for residential/agricultural leases and for camel transport, along with the crucial exception when the parties agree on a deferred payment schedule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two distinct ijarah contracts: lease of house/land and hire of a camel for transport. Note the different objects and benefit structures.
House/land benefit is continuous; transport benefit is segmented by stages of the journey.
2
State the default demand interval
For house/land: wage may be demanded every day. For camel driver: wage may be demanded after each completed stage (marhalah). These are the defaults when payment time is not agreed.
A stage (marhalah) is a unit of distance typically completed in a day’s travel.
3
Recognize the exception for specified time
If the contract explicitly states a payment date or interval (e.g., 'rent after two months'), that term governs and overrides the default rule.
The exception applies equally to both scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولرب الدار والأرض طلب الأجر كل يوم، وللجمال كل مرحلة . ولرب الدار إلخ لأنه منفعة مقصودة، وما دون اليوم لا حد له، فصار كالنفقة لها طلبها عند المساء في كل ساعة، أراد به ما إذا أطلقه، أما إذا بين وقت الاستحقاق في العقد تعين؛ لأنه بمنزلة التعجيل كما إذا قال: آجرتك هذه الدار سنة على أن تعطي الأجرة بعد شهرين [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٨/٧] وللجمال إلخ : أي للجمال أن يطالبه كل مر- مرحلة إذا لم يبين وقت الاستحقاق، فإن بين بأن قال: "بشرط أن أعطي الأجر بعد شهرين" يطالب به بعدهما. (مسكين)
And the owner of the house and land may demand the wage every day, and the camel driver may demand it at every stage. ...
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage states a ruling about the timing of wage payment in ijarah when the contract does not specify a due date. The matn says: the lessor of a house or land may demand rent daily, and the camel driver (for transport) may demand payment after each stage. The commentary explains: the daily demand for rent is because the benefit of a house is a continuous benefit that accrues moment by moment, so the wage is due proportionally. If the contract specifies a time for payment (e.g., monthly), then that governs. Similarly for the camel driver: he can demand wage after each stage unless a deferred payment term is agreed. This ruling establishes default rules for payment intervals in continuous and stage-based ijarah.

Key Terms
المرحلة (al-marhalah): A stage or leg of a journey, used as a unit for wage calculation in transport ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person rents a house for a year and no payment schedule is mentioned, how often can the landlord demand rent?
A) Once at the end of the year.
B) Monthly.
C) Daily.
D) At any time he chooses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, the default payment intervals are daily for property and per stage for transport, unless the contract fixes a different schedule.
