When is Wage Due for Common Workers? – The Case of the Baker, Washer, and Tailor
Ruling on wage entitlement and liability for common workers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for wage becoming wajib for an ajir mushtarak and apply the Hanafi position on baker's liability for burned or stolen bread.

Core Idea
For effect workers, wage is due upon completion and delivery; for the baker, removal from the oven suffices if in the owner's house.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies when common workers (ajir mushtarak) are entitled to their wage. It distinguishes between workers whose work leaves a visible effect (like washer and tailor) and those whose work does not (like baker in certain contexts). It also addresses the baker's liability if the bread burns or is stolen, with a known intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the workers and their work type
Categorize each worker as having 'work with effect' (a trace on the object) or without. The washer and tailor have effect; the baker's work is also effect but with nuance.
Effect workers require delivery; non-effect workers (like transporter) require only completion.
2
Determine when wage is due under normal conditions
For washer/tailor: after finishing work AND delivering. For baker: after removing bread from the oven if baking in the owner's house (counts as delivery). If baking in his own house, delivery is needed.
3
Analyze the baker's liability for burn or theft after removal
If bread burns after removal (in owner's house), baker gets wage and no liability. If stolen after removal but before delivery (baker's own house), there is an ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says no liability (amanah); Sahibayn say baker has a choice.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
For a partial building job, similar principles apply: some Hanafis say wage due for delivered part, others say no wage until full completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللقصار والخياط بعد الفراغ عن عمله وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور، فإن أخرجه فاحترق له الأجر، ولا ضمان. للخباز وللقصار إلخ: أي وللقصار والخياط أن يطالبه بعد الفراغ من عمله؛ لأن العمل في البعض غير منتفع به، فلا يستوجب به الأجر، وأراد به ما إذا سلمه، فأفاد أنه لو هلك في يده قبل التسليم فلا أجر له، وكذا كل من لعمله أثر ، وإن لم يكن لعمله ،أثر ، فكما فرغ منه استحق الأجر، وإن لم يسلمها كالجمال والملاح، فلا يسقط الأجر في الهلاك بعده وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الخياط في بيت المستأجر، فإنه لا يستحق ببعض العمل شيئا؛ لما قدمناه واختاره في "الهداية"، ويتفرع عليه أيضا ما إذا استأجره لبناء داره فبنى البعض، ثم النهدم، فلا أجر له، ولا يستحق الأجر على البعض إلا في سكنى الدار وقطع المسافة، واختار جماعة من مشايخنا خلافه، ومسألة البناء منصوص عليها في الأصل أنه يجب الأجر بالبعض؛ لكونه مسلما إلى المستأجر، ونقله الكرخي عن أصحابنا، وجزم به في غاية البيان" ردا على "الهداية"، فكان هو المذهب، ولهذا اختاره المصنف في "المستصفى" وإن كانت عبارته هنا مطلقة البحر الرائق: ٤٣٨/٧] وللخباز إلخ لأن تمام العمل بالإخراج، أطلقه، فأفاد أنه يستحق بإخراج البعض بقدره؛ لأن العمل في ذلك القدر صار مسلما إلى صاحب الدقيق كذا في "غاية "البيان" و "الجوهرة" ، ومراده إذا كان الخبز في بيت المستأجر؛ لأنه صار مسلما إليه بمجرد الإخراج كما صرح به في "مستصفاه" ، أما إذا كان خارجا عن بيت المستأجر، سواء كان في بيت الخباز أو لا، فلا يستحق الأجرة إلا بالتسليم ،حقيقة وفي "الجوهرة": فإن سرق الخبز بعد ما أخرجه فإن كان يخبز في بيت صاحب الطعام فله الأجرة وإن كان يخبز في بيت الخباز فلا أجرة له؛ لعدم التسليم، ولا ضمان عليه فيما سرق عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه في يده أمانة خلافا لهما، وهي . مسألة الأجير المشترك. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٨/٧] فإن أخرجه إلخ لأنه صار مسلما بالوضع في بيته، فاستحق المسمى، ولم يوجد منه جناية، فلا ضمان عليه إجماعا، فأفاد أنه لو كان الخبز في غير بيت المستأجر فاحترق فلا أجر له ولا ضمان عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: إن شاء ضمنه دقيقا مثل دقيقه ولا أجر له وإن شاء ضمنه قيمة الخبز، وأعطاه الأجر، ولا يجب عليه ضمان الحطب والملح، وقيد بكونه احترق عقيب الإخراج؛ لأنه إذا احترق قبل الإخراج، فعليه الضمان في قول أصحابنا جميعا؛ لأنه مما جنته يداه بتقصيره في القلع من التنور، فإن ضمنه قيمته مخبوزا أعطاه الأجر، وإن ضمنه دقيقا لم يكن له أجر ، كذا في غاية البيان". [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٩/٧] 6 ولا ضمان أي على الخباز إذا كان يخبز في بيت المستأجر بالإجماع عند أصحابنا الثلاثة؛ لأنه هلك بعد التسليم كذا قال في "البحر" و"العيني" وغيرهما، ولم يذكروا فيه خلافا، وقال في "ملا" "مسكين" و "منحة الخالق على البحر الرائق" لابن عابدين: إن فيه خلافا، قال في "ملا مسكين": وذكر القدوري في "شرحه : أن على قولهما يجب الضمان، وقال في "منحة الخالق": أقول في الجامع الصغير وشروحه أطلقوا الجواب بعدم الضمان، ولم يذكروا الخلاف، فعن هذا قالوا: الجواب بحرى على عمومه، أما عنده فلأنه لم يهلك من عمله، وأما عندهما فلأنه هلك بعد التسليم -
And for the washer and tailor after finishing his work, and for the baker after removing the bread from the oven. If he removes it and it burns, he gets the wage and no liability. ...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage covers when workers known as 'ajir mushtarak (common workers) become entitled to their wage. The matn states: the washer (qassar) and tailor are entitled to wage after completing the work; the baker after removing the bread from the oven. If the baker removes the bread and it burns, he receives his wage and bears no liability for the burn. The commentary discusses: for workers whose work leaves a visible effect (like tailoring), wage is due only upon completion and delivery. For those whose work has no lasting effect (like transport), wage is due upon completion even without delivery. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether partial work (e.g., partial building) entitles partial wage. Some say yes if delivered, others no. For the baker: removing bread from the oven completes the work. If he bakes in the owner's house, removal constitutes delivery, so he gets wage and is not liable for subsequent theft or burning. If baking in his own house, he gets wage only upon actual delivery. There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn about liability for stolen bread: Abu Hanifa says no liability because it is an amanah; the Sahibayn say he must compensate if he chooses to take wage or give up wage and compensate with flour. The relied view is the one in the Fatwa.

Key Terms
القصار (al-qassar): A washer/cleaner of clothes, a common worker whose work has an effect on the object.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A common worker hired for a lump sum to perform a specific task, not for a period.
التسليم (al-taslim): Delivery of the finished object to the employer, which triggers wage obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied (mufta bihi) position, if a baker bakes bread in his own house, removes it from the oven, and then the bread is stolen before the owner picks it up, what is the baker's entitlement and liability?
A) He gets full wage and no liability.
B) He gets no wage and no liability.
C) He gets no wage and must compensate with flour.
D) He gets wage if he compensates for the bread.

Key Takeaway
Wage for a common worker becomes wajib only upon completion and delivery; for the baker, removal from the oven in the owner's house suffices as delivery, and the relied position is that the baker is not liable for subsequent loss.

When Launderers and Tailors Earn Their Wages
Clarifying when craftsmen with visible work earn wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when workers with visible effect become entitled to wages, identify the condition of delivery, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on partial delivery.

Core Idea
For workers whose work has a visible effect, wage is due only upon complete delivery to the hirer.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi ijara: the entitlement to wages for workers like launderers and tailors. Unlike transporters who earn upon completing the work, these workers must also deliver the finished item. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its sharh clarifies the rule and introduces a dispute among Hanafi scholars about partial delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its basis
Read the core ruling: launderers, tailors, and bakers earn wages only after completing the work and delivering the item. Understand the rationale: partial work provides no benefit to the hirer.
The rule applies to all workers whose work leaves a visible effect (e.g., washing, sewing, building).
2
Distinguish workers without visible effect
Note the exception: camel drivers and sailors earn wages upon completion of work even without delivery. Their work has no tangible result; the benefit is the service itself.
This distinction is crucial for applying the correct rule.
3
Explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on partial delivery
Read the dispute: al-Hidayah holds that no wage is due for partial work (e.g., building part of a wall that collapses). Al-Karkhi and others counter that delivery of a part is beneficial, thus entitling the worker to wage for the delivered portion.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) supports wage for delivered part, as chosen by al-Nasafi in al-Mustasfa.
4
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Test your understanding: a tailor sews a shirt, but the customer never picks it up, and the shirt is ruined in the tailor's shop. Is the tailor entitled to wage? Why?
Answer: No, because delivery did not occur. The washing example from the passage is analogous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
أحكام الإجارة
وللقصار والخياط بعد الفراغ عن عمله وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور، فإن أخرجه فاحترق له الأجر، ولا ضمان.
وللقصار إلخ: أي وللقصار والخياط أن يطالبه بعد الفراغ من عمله؛ لأن العمل في البعض غير منتفع به، فلا يستوجب به الأجر، وأراد به ما إذا سلمه، فأفاد أنه لو هلك في يده قبل التسليم فلا أجر له، وكذا كل من لعمله أثر ، وإن لم يكن لعمله أثر ، فكما فرغ منه استحق الأجر، وإن لم يسلمها كالجمال والملاح، فلا يسقط الأجر في الهلاك بعده وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الخياط في بيت المستأجر، فإنه لا يستحق ببعض العمل شيئا؛ لما قدمناه واختاره في "الهداية"، ويتفرع عليه أيضا ما إذا استأجره لبناء داره فبنى البعض، ثم النهدم، فلا أجر له، ولا يستحق الأجر على البعض إلا في سكنى الدار وقطع المسافة، واختار جماعة من مشايخنا خلافه، ومسألة البناء منصوص عليها في الأصل أنه يجب الأجر بالبعض؛ لكونه مسلما إلى المستأجر، ونقله الكرخي عن أصحابنا، وجزم به في غاية البيان" ردا على "الهداية"، فكان هو المذهب، ولهذا اختاره المصنف في "المستصفى" وإن كانت عبارته هنا مطلقة البحر الرائق: ٤٣٨/٧]
Book of Hiring. Rulings of Hiring. For the launderer and the tailor after completion of his work, and for the baker after taking out the bread from the oven; if he takes it out and it burns, he gets the wage, and no liability. 'For the launderer etc.': meaning that the launderer and the tailor can demand (wages) after completion of his work, because work on part (of the item) is not beneficial, so he does not deserve wage for it. And by it (the author) meant when he delivers it (the finished item). So it indicates that if it perishes in his hand before delivery, then no wage for him. Similarly, everyone whose work has an effect (visible result), while if his work has no effect, then as soon as he finishes it he deserves the wage even if he does not deliver it, like the camel driver and the sailor; so the wage does not fall away due to destruction after that. And he (the author) gave it absolutely (unrestricted), so it includes the case when the tailor is in the house of the hirer: he does not deserve anything for partial work, for what we have mentioned; and this is chosen in al-Hidayah. And it also branches out from it the case if he hires him to build his house, and he builds part, then it collapses, then no wage for him. And he does not deserve wage for part except in dwelling in the house and covering the distance (i.e., hire of a mount). And a group of our scholars chose contrary to that. And the issue of building is stated in the original (source) that wage is due for part because it has been delivered to the hirer, and al-Karkhi transmitted this from our companions, and it is determined in Ghayat al-Bayan in refutation of al-Hidayah, so that is the madhhab, and for this the author chose it in al-Mustasfa, although his expression here is absolute. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/438]
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its sharh addresses the ruling for hired workers whose work produces a visible effect (like washing, tailoring, building). The key principle is that such workers are entitled to their full wage only upon complete delivery of the finished item. Partial work is not beneficial to the hirer, so no wage is due for it. If the item perishes in the worker's hands before delivery, he forfeits his wage. This contrasts with workers whose work has no tangible effect (like transporters), who earn wages upon completion of the work regardless of delivery. The commentary also discusses a dispute regarding building: if a builder builds part of a wall and it collapses, some scholars (including al-Quduri and al-Karkhi) hold that he deserves wage for the part delivered, opposing the view of al-Hidayah. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq (al-Nasafi) preferred the view that wage is due for delivered parts, as stated in his Mustasfa.

Key Terms
القصار (al-qassar): The launderer or washerman who cleans clothes.
الخياط (al-khayyat): The tailor who sews cloth into garments.
التسليم (al-taslim): Physical delivery of the finished item to the hirer, which triggers entitlement to wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a launderer not deserve any wage if the garment perishes in his hand before he returns it to the owner?
A) Because the launderer is an ajir khas (specific hire) and bears all risk
B) Because the work is not yet delivered, so no benefit has accrued to the hirer
C) Because the launderer must be paid only after one month
D) Because the garment is still owned by the launderer until delivery

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, workers whose work has a visible effect earn wages only upon delivery of the completed item to the hirer, with an internal ikhtilaf on whether partial delivery also triggers entitlement.

6 min
Baker's Wage Entitlement and Liability After Removal from Oven
Ruling with proof on baker's wage and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a baker earns his wage and apply the Hanafi ruling on his liability for theft or burning of the bread.

Core Idea
Removal from oven in hirer's house = delivery; baker not liable thereafter.

In this lesson, we examine the rules governing a hired baker (khabbāz), focusing on when his work is considered complete for wage entitlement and what liability he bears if the bread is stolen or burned. The central distinction is whether the baking occurs in the hirer's house or elsewhere. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on theft liability before delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the baker's work (removing bread from oven). The ruling distinguishes between wage entitlement and liability for loss. Wage becomes wajib upon completion of work (removal) only if the bread is delivered.
Completion alone does not entitle wage; delivery is key.
2
Distinguish based on location of baking
If baking in hirer's house, removal from oven constitutes delivery (taslīm), so baker earns wage and holds bread as amana (no liability for theft/burning unless negligence). If baking elsewhere (e.g., baker's house), baker must physically deliver bread to earn wage; until delivery, he bears liability.
This distinction is the pivot of the ruling.
3
Apply the amana principle (ajir mushtarak)
The baker is an ajir mushtarak (shared worker), meaning he is not liable for loss unless negligent. Abu Hanifa applies this strictly: no liability for theft even before delivery. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold the baker liable for theft before delivery because he has not completed delivery.
This ikhtilaf is rooted in different views on when liability transfers.
4
Analyse the scenario of burning after removal
If bread burns immediately after removal (but before physical delivery), the ruling depends on location. If in hirer's house, no liability by consensus because delivery occurred. If elsewhere, Abu Hanifa says no liability (amana); the two companions give the hirer an option to claim compensation in flour or value, adjusting wage accordingly.
Burning before removal always imposes liability due to negligence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللخباز إلخ لأن تمام العمل بالإخراج، أطلقه، فأفاد أنه يستحق بإخراج البعض بقدره؛ لأن العمل في ذلك القدر صار مسلما إلى صاحب الدقيق كذا في "غاية البيان" و "الجوهرة" ، ومراده إذا كان الخبز في بيت المستأجر؛ لأنه صار مسلما إليه بمجرد الإخراج كما صرح به في "مستصفاه" ، أما إذا كان خارجا عن بيت المستأجر، سواء كان في بيت الخباز أو لا، فلا يستحق الأجرة إلا بالتسليم حقيقة وفي "الجوهرة": فإن سرق الخبز بعد ما أخرجه فإن كان يخبز في بيت صاحب الطعام فله الأجرة وإن كان يخبز في بيت الخباز فلا أجرة له؛ لعدم التسليم، ولا ضمان عليه فيما سرق عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه في يده أمانة خلافا لهما، وهي مسألة الأجير المشترك. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٨/٧] فإن أخرجه إلخ لأنه صار مسلما بالوضع في بيته، فاستحق المسمى، ولم يوجد منه جناية، فلا ضمان عليه إجماعا، فأفاد أنه لو كان الخبز في غير بيت المستأجر فاحترق فلا أجر له ولا ضمان عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: إن شاء ضمنه دقيقا مثل دقيقه ولا أجر له وإن شاء ضمنه قيمة الخبز، وأعطاه الأجر، ولا يجب عليه ضمان الحطب والملح، وقيد بكونه احترق عقيب الإخراج؛ لأنه إذا احترق قبل الإخراج، فعليه الضمان في قول أصحابنا جميعا؛ لأنه مما جنته يداه بتقصيره في القلع من التنور، فإن ضمنه قيمته مخبوزا أعطاه الأجر، وإن ضمنه دقيقا لم يكن له أجر، كذا في غاية البيان. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٩/٧] ولا ضمان أي على الخباز إذا كان يخبز في بيت المستأجر بالإجماع عند أصحابنا الثلاثة؛ لأنه هلك بعد التسليم كذا قال في "البحر" و"العيني" وغيرهما، ولم يذكروا فيه خلافا، وقال في "ملا مسكين" و "منحة الخالق على البحر الرائق" لابن عابدين: إن فيه خلافا، قال في "ملا مسكين": وذكر القدوري في "شرحه: أن على قولهما يجب الضمان، وقال في "منحة الخالق": أقول في الجامع الصغير وشروحه أطلقوا الجواب بعدم الضمان، ولم يذكروا الخلاف، فعن هذا قالوا: الجواب بحرى على عمومه، أما عنده فلأنه لم يهلك من عمله، وأما عندهما فلأنه هلك بعد التسليم = وإنما ذكر الخلاف القدوري برواية ابن سماعة عن محمد إلخ وقال في "فتح الله المعين": إن هذا هو اختيار القدوري، وأما عند غيره فنفي الضمان مجرى على عمومه، فوجه عدم الضمان عنده أنه لم يهلك من عمله، وأما على قولهما فلأنه هلك بعد التسليم، وهذا يتم إن كان الوضع في بيته تسليما قاله في "العناية" بعد العزو إلى "النهاية".
'For the baker etc.' because completion of the work is by removal (from the oven); he (the author) gave it unrestrictedly, so it indicates that he deserves (wage) for removal of part proportionally, because the work on that amount has become delivered to the owner of the flour. So in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Jawhara, and his intent is when the bread is in the house of the hirer, because it becomes delivered to him simply by removal, as he stated in his Mustasfa. But if it is outside the hirer's house, whether in the baker's house or not, he does not deserve the wage except by actual delivery. And in al-Jawhara: if the bread is stolen after he removed it, then if he bakes in the house of the food owner, he gets the wage; but if he bakes in the baker's house, no wage for him due to lack of delivery. And there is no liability on him for what was stolen, according to Abu Hanifa, because it is an amana in his hand, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This is the issue of the ajir mushtarak (shared worker). [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/438] 'If he takes it out etc.' because it becomes delivered by placing it in his (the hirer's) house, so he deserves the named wage, and no offense came from him, so no liability on him by consensus. So it indicates that if the bread was in other than the hirer's house and burned, then no wage for him and no liability according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (the two companions): if he wishes, he compensates with flour like his flour and no wage for him; and if he wishes, he compensates with the value of bread and gives him the wage. And he is not liable to compensate for firewood and salt. And it is restricted to when it burns immediately after removal, because if it burns before removal, then he is liable in the saying of all our companions, because it is from the offense of his hands due to negligence in pulling it out of the oven. Then if he compensates its value as baked, he gives him the wage; and if he compensates as flour, he has no wage. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7/439] And 'no liability' means on the baker when he bakes in the hirer's house, by consensus among our three imams, because it perished after delivery. So said in al-Bahr and al-Ayni and others, and they did not mention any disagreement. But in 'Mulla Miskin' and 'Minhah al-Khaliq 'ala al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' by Ibn Abidin: there is disagreement. He said in Mulla Miskin: al-Quduri mentioned in his Sharh that according to them (the two companions) liability is obligatory. And in Minhah al-Khaliq: I say in al-Jami' al-Saghir and its commentaries they gave the answer of non-liability unrestrictedly, and did not mention the disagreement. For this reason they said: the answer runs on its generality. As for him (Abu Hanifa), because it did not perish from his work; and as for them (the two companions), because it perished after delivery. = And al-Quduri mentioned the disagreement by a riwaya from Ibn Sama'ah from Muhammad etc. And said in Fath Allah al-Mu'in: this is the choice of al-Quduri. But according to others, negation of liability runs on its generality. So the face of non-liability according to him is that it did not perish from his work; and according to them, because it perished after delivery. And this is completed if placing in his house is delivery, as said in al-Inayah after referring to al-Nihayah.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq elaborates the ruling for a hired baker. The central issue is when the baker's work is considered complete for the purpose of earning wages, and what his liability is if the bread is stolen or burned. The rule distinguishes based on where the baking takes place. If the baker works in the hirer's house, the bread is considered delivered immediately upon removal from the oven, so he earns his wage and bears no liability for subsequent loss. If he works elsewhere, he must physically deliver the bread to earn his wage. There is also a discussion of the baker as an ajir mushtarak (shared worker) and the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding liability for theft: Abu Hanifa holds no liability because the baker is an amana holder, while the companions hold liability. The text also covers the case of burning before removal (negligence) and the compensation options.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A worker who is hired to work for multiple people or for the public, not exclusively for one hirer; his liability is that of an amana holder.
التسليم (al-taslim): Physical delivery of the baked bread to the hirer, which triggers wage entitlement and ends liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A baker bakes bread in the hirer's house. After removing from the oven, the bread is stolen. According to Abu Hanifa, what is the baker's liability?
A) He must compensate with flour of similar quality
B) He must compensate with the value of baked bread
C) He is not liable because the bread was delivered by removal
D) He is liable because the theft is due to his negligence

Key Takeaway
The baker's wage entitlement and liability hinge on delivery (taslim), which occurs by removal from the oven if baking is in the hirer's house, and the baker as an ajir mushtarak is not liable for theft or burning after delivery.

When a Cook Earns His Wage and His Liability for Spoilage
Defining when a hired cook's wage is due (after serving) and liability for spoilage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a hired cook's wage becomes due according to the Hanafi school and explain the cook's liability for spoilage and accidental fire.

Core Idea
A cook's wage is due after serving (gharf) in feasts; for other meals, custom decides, but he remains liable for spoilage, not accidental fire.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies two practical matters in the hiring of a cook: first, the point at which his wage becomes due, and second, his liability if food is spoiled or a fire caused. There is an internal Hanafi dispute on the first point: does he earn his wage upon cooking or upon serving? The author (al-Nasafi) states it is after serving without restriction, but al-Quduri restricted it to wedding feasts. The commentator in al-Bahr explains that custom is the basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the cook's wage becomes wajib after gharf (serving the food onto dishes). This is the completion of his work for the purpose of wage entitlement.
Note that gharf is defined as extracting broth from pot to bowls.
2
Determine the scope of the ruling
Al-Nasafi gives an unqualified statement, while al-Quduri restricts it to wedding feasts. The commentator in al-Bahr argues that the author's statement covers all occasions except household food, relying on custom (urf) to distinguish.
Custom may define the completion point for non-feast meals.
3
Examine the customary principle
The passage implies that for family meals, custom may not require serving; thus the cook's wage is due upon cooking. The author's lack of restriction is justified as a reference to custom.
Custom is a recognized source in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the liability rules
If the cook spoils, burns, or undercooks the food, he is liable (damages). However, if he causes an accidental fire (e.g., a spark) while permitted to use fire, he is not liable, similar to digging a well on one's property.
Liability for spoilage is strict but for fire it is excused due to permission.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
For a wedding feast, wage is due after gharf. For a daily family meal, custom determines. For spoilage, the cook compensates; for accidental fire, he does not.
Always consider local custom for non-feast situations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللطباخ بعد الغرف، وللبان بعد الإقامة، يعني
بعد الغرف: إذا استأجر طباخا ليطبخ له الطعام، فالغرف أي إخراج المرق من القدر إلى القصاع عليه، وهذا في طعام الوليمة، وأما إذا استأجره ليطبخ طعام نفسه خاصة، فالغرف ليس عليه، فكان ينبغي للمصنف أن يقيده بطعام الوليمة كما قيده القدوري، قال في "البحر" اعتذارا عن المصنف: إنه لم يقيده؛ لأنه يرد عليه بقية أنواع الأطعمة مثل الوكيرة أي طعام البناء، والخرس أي طعام الولادة وغيرهما، ولا يرد عليه طعام أهل بيته؛ لأن العرف أنه لا يحتاج إلى طباخ فلا حاجة إلى إخراجه أقول : من قيده بطعام الوليمة عنى به جميع أنواع الأطعمة سوى طعام أهل بيته، فلا يتوجه الإيراد بباقي الأطعمة في صورة التقييد، نعم، عدم تقييد المصنف إحالة على العرف بإخراج طعام أهل بيته صحيح. [٤٣٩/٧] قال في "البحر": وإن أفسد الطباخ الطعام أو أحرقه أو لم ينضجه فهو ضامن، وإذا دخل الخباز أو الطباخ بنار ليخبز أو يطبخ بها ، فوقعت منه شرارة، فاحترق البيت فلا ضمان عليه؛ لأنه مأذون في إدخال النار، وكذا لا ضمان على صاحب الدار إذا احترق شيء من السكان في الدار؛ لأنه لم يكن متعديا في هذا السبب كمن حفر بئرا في ملكه. [٤٣٩/٧]
'And for the cook after serving (gharf), and for the brick-maker after setting (iqamah), meaning...' 'After serving: if he hires a cook to cook food for him, then serving is extracting the broth from the pot into the bowls, and this applies to wedding feast food. But if he hires him to cook his own family food specifically, then serving is not upon him. So it would have been appropriate for the author to restrict it to wedding feast food as al-Quduri restricted it. He said in al-Bahr, apologizing for the author: he did not restrict it because other types of food occur to him, such as al-wakirah (food for building), al-khurs (food for childbirth), etc. And food of his own household does not occur, because the custom is that he does not need a cook, so there is no need to bring it out. I say: whoever restricts it to wedding feast means all types of food except his household food, so the objection against the other foods in the case of restriction is not directed. Yes, the author's lack of restriction is a reference to custom regarding excluding his household food, correct. [7/439] He said in al-Bahr: If the cook spoils the food or burns it or does not cook it thoroughly, he is liable. And if the baker or cook enters with fire to bake or cook with it, and a spark falls from him and the house burns, there is no liability on him, because he is permitted to bring in the fire. Similarly, no liability on the owner of the house if something of the residents in the house burns, because he was not transgressing in this cause, like one who digs a well in his property. [7/439]
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage addresses the hired cook. The general rule is that a cook earns his wage after serving (gharf), i.e., transferring the food from the pot to the serving dishes. However, this applies primarily to feasts (like wedding feasts), where such service is customary. For everyday family meals, the custom may be that the cook's work is complete upon cooking, and serving is not expected. The author (al-Nasafi) did not restrict to feasts, but al-Quduri did. The commentator in al-Bahr argues that the author's unqualified statement covers all occasions except household food. The passage also covers the cook's liability: if he spoils, burns, or undercooks the food, he is liable. However, if he causes a fire accidentally (e.g., sparks), he is not liable because he was authorized to use fire.

Key Terms
الغرف (al-gharf): Serving the cooked food by transferring it from pot to dishes, considered the completion of work for a cook in feast contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a hired cook for a wedding feast become entitled to his full wage?
A) As soon as he finishes cooking
B) After he serves the food (gharf)
C) After the guests finish eating
D) After he is paid by the host

Key Takeaway
A cook's wage becomes wajib after completing the agreed service (gharf for feasts), and he is liable for spoilage but not for accidental fire while authorized.

When a Brick-Maker Earns His Wage
Clarifying the completion of work for brick-maker and the intra-Hanafi dispute on tashrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on when a brick-maker's wage becomes due and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The brick-maker's wage is due upon stacking, not just drying, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

In hiring a brick-maker, the moment his wage becomes wajib depends on what constitutes completion of the work. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa considers setting the bricks upright (iqamah) sufficient, but the two companions require stacking (tashrij). The fatwa is on their view. Understanding this dispute illuminates how the Hanafi school resolves differences between its founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
Abu Hanifa holds that wage is due upon iqamah (setting bricks to dry). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require tashrij (stacking). A third view (al-Mustasfa) requires delivery.
2
Follow each party's reasoning
Abu Hanifa: iqamah makes the bricks transportable and usable, so work is done. The companions: tashrij protects bricks from damage and is customary completion.
The text notes that before iqamah the clay is scattered, and bread analogy shows need for removal.
3
Analyze the practical consequence
If bricks are lost after iqamah but before tashrij, loss falls on the hirer (Abu Hanifa) or the worker (companions).
This thamarah al-khilaf highlights the difference in practice.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Durr from al-Kamal states fatwa is on the saying of the two companions.
The relied-upon view is that tashrij is required for wage entitlement.
5
Note the third position
The author of al-Mustasfa stipulates delivery without counting when bricks are made on the hirer's property.
Al-Bahr considers this preferable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللبان: أي الذي يتخذ اللبن من الطين وإنما تصح الإجارة بشرط تعيين الملبن، فلو لم يعين ولهم ملابن تستعمل على سواء فسدت الإجارة، فلو لم يكن لهم إلا ملبن واحد أو متعدد لكن يغلب استعمالهم لواحد منها، "قهستاني". (عيني، فتح) صحت بعد الإقامة: أي إن استأجر لبانا ليضرب له لبنا في ملكه، فهو يستحق الأجر إذا أقام اللبن عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن العمل تم بالإقامة، وعندهما لا يستحقه حتى يشرجه؛ لأن التشريج من تمام العمل، ولا يؤمن عليه من الفساد قبله وبقولهما يفتى كذا في "الدر" عن الكمال والإقامة النصب بعد الجفاف والتشريج أن يركب بعضه على بعض، هذا إذا ضرب اللبن في ملك المستأجر، وإن ضرب في ملك نفسه فلا يجب الأجر عنده إلا بالعد عليه بعد إقامته، وعندهما بالعد عليه بعد التشريج، و لم يشترط المصنف في "المستصفى" العد إذا لم يكن في ملك المستأجر بل شرط التسليم، قال في "البحر" [٤٤٠/٧] : وهو الأولى؛ لأنه لو سلمه بغير عد كان له الأجر كما لا يخفى. والحاصل أن العمل عند أبي حنيفة محله قد تم بعد الإقامة والتشريج أمر زائد كالنقل، ألا ترى أنه ينتفع به قبل التشريج بالنقل إلى موضع العمل، بخلاف ما قبل الإقامة؛ لأنه طين منتشر، وبخلاف الخبز؛ لأنه غير منتفع به قبل الإخراج، وفائدة الخلاف فيما إذا تلف قبل التشريج بعد الإقامة، فعنده تلف من مال المستأجر، وعندهما: من مال الأجير. هذا ملخص ما في الشروح والحواشي)
'And for the brick-maker: i.e., the one who makes bricks from clay. And the hire contract is valid only on condition of specifying the mold (malban). If he does not specify and they have molds used equally, the hire is invalid. If they have only one mold or multiple but their use is predominantly for one of them, (Qahistani) (Ayni, Fath) it is valid. 'After setting (iqamah)': i.e., if he hires a brick-maker to beat bricks for him in his (the hirer's) property, then he deserves the wage when he sets the bricks according to Abu Hanifa, because the work is completed by setting. According to them (the two companions), he does not deserve it until he stacks them (yusharrij), because stacking is part of the complete work, and it is not safe from corruption before it. And according to their saying is the fatwa, as in al-Durr from al-Kamal. And 'iqamah' is the erection after drying, and 'tashrij' is to pile some on top of others. This is when he beats bricks in the hirer's property. And if he beats in his own property, then wage is not obligatory according to him (Abu Hanifa) except by counting them after his iqamah, and according to them by counting after tashrij. And the author in al-Mustasfa did not stipulate counting when not in the hirer's property, but stipulated delivery. He said in al-Bahr [7/440]: that is better, because if he delivers without counting, he deserves the wage, as is not hidden. The summary: the work according to Abu Hanifa is completed after iqamah, and tashrij is an extra thing like transportation. Do you not see that benefit is taken before tashrij by transporting to the work place, unlike before iqamah because it is scattered mud, and unlike bread because it is not beneficial before removal from oven. And the fruit of the dispute is when it perishes before tashrij after iqamah: according to him, it perishes from the property of the hirer; according to them, from the property of the worker. This is the summary from the commentaries and glosses.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage discusses the brick-maker (labban) who makes bricks from clay. It first notes a condition for the validity of his hire: the mold (malban) must be specified. Then it addresses the moment when his wage is due. There is a known intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the work is completed and wage is due once the bricks are set to dry (iqamah), because the bricks are then beneficial (can be moved). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that stacking (tashrij) is also necessary because the bricks are not yet safe from damage. The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the two companions. The passage also distinguishes between working on the hirer's property and on the worker's own property, and the role of counting or delivery in the latter case. The practical consequence of this dispute is seen in loss: if bricks perish after iqamah but before tashrij, Abu Hanifa says the loss falls on the hirer (since wage is already earned), while the companions say it falls on the worker (since wage not yet earned).

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqamah): Setting the bricks upright to dry after molding.
التشريج (al-tashrij): Stacking the dried bricks on top of each other.
الملبن (al-malban): The mold used for making bricks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does a brick-maker earn his wage?
A) After setting the bricks to dry (iqamah)
B) After stacking the bricks (tashrij)
C) After the bricks are delivered to the hirer
D) After the bricks are counted

Key Takeaway
For a brick-maker's hire, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that wage becomes wajib only after stacking (tashrij), and any loss before that is borne by the worker.

Craftsman's Right of Retention: Conditions and Proof
States the rule of retention for effect-bearing work and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a craftsman to retain the object for his wage and explain the qiyas argument supporting the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
A craftsman may detain the object only if the wage is immediate and work done on his own premises.

This passage addresses a practical problem: can a tailor, dyer, or fuller hold onto a customer's garment until paid? The Hanafi school recognizes a right of retention based on analogy to sale, but only under strict conditions. We will analyze the rule, its conditions, and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the craftsman's right to retain the object (habs). What is the hukm level? It is a permissible legal right (mubah), not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas to sale: the contracted matter (the effect) is a quality subsisting in the object, so retaining it to secure payment is analogous to a seller holding the sold item until payment.
Qiyas jaliy because the illa is clear: both involve a subsisting right to a countervalue.
3
Identify the conditions
The right exists only if (1) the wage is immediate (spot payment) and (2) the work is done in the craftsman's own premises. If either condition is absent, no right of retention.
Justifications: for deferred wage, payment not due immediately so no right to detain; for work in hirer's premises, the object is already in the owner's possession.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar denies the right of retention entirely. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa's view) is the mufta bihi. The practical consequence: in Zufar's view, the craftsman must deliver the work and then pursue payment separately.
The text states 'عندنا' (according to us) to assert the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لعمله أثر في العين كالصباغ والقصار يحبسها للأجير فإن حبس فضاع، فلا ضمان ولا أجر. قوله: لعمله أثر إلخ: أي إذا كان للأجير أثر في عمل فله أن يحبسه حتى يستوفي الأجر عندنا، خلافا لزفر بحاله؛ لأن المعقود عليه وصف قائم في الثوب، فله حق الحبس لاستيفاء البدل كما في البيع، وهذا إذا كان عمله في بيته، والأجر حالا، وأما إذا كان الأجر مؤجلا أو العمل في بيت المستأجر، فليس له حق الحبس، وجه الأول: أن تسليم الأجر ليس بواجب عليه في الحال، فلا يملك الحبس كما لو باع بثمن مؤجل ليس له الحبس، ووجه الثاني: أن المتاع وقع مسلما إلى المالك؛ لكون المحل في يده، وهو ضامن لما جنت يداه عند الإمام وإن كان في بيت المستأجر، بخلاف الملاح إذا غرقت السفينة بمده، وصاحب المتاع فيها، حيث لا يضمن المتاع؛ لأنه في يد مالكه حقيقة والمد تصرف في السفينة دون المتاع، فكان مأذونا فيه من قبل المالك، فلم يكن متعديا، فلا يؤاخذ بالضمان. كذا في الفتح والبحر ملخصا
For his work has an effect in the object, like the dyer and the fuller, he may detain it for the hirer. If he detains and it is lost, then no guarantee and no wage. He said: 'For his work has an effect etc.': meaning if the hired person has an effect in the work, he may detain it until he receives the wage according to us, contrary to Zufar in his case; because the contracted object is a quality subsisting in the garment, so he has the right of retention to receive the substitute, as in sale. This is if his work is in his house and the wage is immediate. As for if the wage is deferred or the work is in the hirer's house, he has no right of retention. The justification of the first: that delivery of the wage is not obligatory upon him immediately, so he does not possess the right of retention, just as if he sold for a deferred price, he has no retention. The justification of the second: that the commodity has been handed over to the owner, because the place is in his hand, and he is liable for what his hands have inflicted according to the Imam, even if in the hirer's house, unlike the sailor if the ship sinks due to his pulling and the owner of the commodity is in it, where he does not guarantee the commodity; because it is in the hand of its owner in reality, and the pulling is an action on the ship not on the commodity, so he was permitted by the owner, so he was not transgressing, so he is not taken to task for guarantee. Thus in Al-Fath and Al-Bahr, summarized.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute explaining the rule of retention for craftsmen. The matn states the general principle: a hired person whose work leaves an effect on the object (like dyer, fuller) may detain it for his wage; if he detains and it is lost, he is neither liable nor entitled to the wage. The commentary expands: the hired person has the right to detain until the wage is paid, opposing Zufar. The reason is that the contracted matter (the effect) is a quality subsisting in the garment, so he has a right to hold it as a security, analogous to a seller holding the sold item until payment. However, this right is conditional: the work must be done in the craftsman's own premises and the wage must be immediate (spot payment). If the wage is deferred or the work is done in the hirer's premises, the right does not exist. The commentary justifies each condition: for deferred wage, the hirer is not obliged to pay immediately, so the craftsman cannot detain; for work in the hirer's house, the object is already in the owner's possession, and the craftsman is liable for his actions even there, unlike the sailor who is not liable for damage to cargo because he acts only on the ship with permission. The passage concludes by citing Al-Fath and Al-Bahr.

Key Terms
الأجر (al-ajr): The wage or fee for the hired work.
الحبس (al-habs): The right of the hired person to retain the object until payment of the wage.
الأجر حالا (al-ajr hālan): Immediate payment of the wage (spot) as opposed to deferred.
الصباغ (al-ṣabbāgh): Dyer – a craftsman who dyes cloth.
القصار (al-qaṣṣār): Fuller – a craftsman who cleans and thickens cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition does a dyer have the right to detain the garment for his wage?
A) When the wage is deferred.
B) When the work is done in the hirer's house.
C) When the wage is immediate and work is done in his own house.
D) Always, regardless of circumstances.

Key Takeaway
A craftsman may detain the object only if the wage is immediate and work is done on his own premises; otherwise, no right of retention.

Fuller's Right of Retention: Does Removing Dirt Count as Creating an Effect?
Dispute on whether removing dirt counts as creating an effect for retention rights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two views on the fuller's right of retention when only removing dirt and identify the mufta bihi position within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Removing hidden dirt does not create a new effect – the preferred view denies the fuller's right to detain.

This lesson examines a subtle but important point in the law of hire (ijāra): when does a craftsman acquire the right to retain the object of his work until paid? The passage focuses on the fuller, a cloth cleaner, and distinguishes between work that adds a new quality (like dyeing) versus work that merely reveals what was hidden (like removing dirt). Within the Hanafi school, the later authorities differed on whether the latter qualifies as creating an 'effect' (athar) that justifies retention. Understanding this dispute reveals how later Hanafi jurists (mutākhkhirūn) practiced tarjīḥ among variant transmissions, and what factors they considered decisive.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of fuller work
First, identify the two categories: (1) work that introduces a new color or substance (e.g., dyeing, starching) – this clearly creates an effect. (2) work that only removes dirt to reveal the cloth's natural whiteness – this is the disputed case.
The word 'effect' (athar) is key: a new attribute vs. uncovering an existing one.
2
State the agreed ruling for the first category
For the first category, there is consensus (ittifāq) that the fuller has the right to retain the garment until his wage is paid, because his work directly creates a new quality in the cloth.
This is the baseline ruling from which the dispute departs.
3
Identify the disputed scenario and the two opinions
For the second category – only removing dirt – there is no agreement. Qādī Khān corrects (ṣaḥḥaḥa) that the fuller does have the right, reasoning that the whiteness was hidden and now appears due to his action, as if he produced it. Al-Nasafī in his Mustaṣfā, citing al-Dhakhīra, corrects that the fuller does NOT have the right, because the whiteness was inherent and he merely removed an obstacle.
The dispute is purely about the legal characterization of the same physical act.
4
Understand the basis for the preferred view
Al-Baḥr recommends giving preference (tarjīḥ) to the denial of the right, and the author of al-Hidāya affirms this. The key reasoning: the whiteness did not come into existence through the fuller's work; it was always present but hidden. Thus, no new attribute (ṣifa) was created, so the condition for retention is not met.
This is the muftā bihi (operative) position in the school.
5
Recognize the process of tashīḥ among later authorities
The passage explicitly shows that later Hanafi scholars (mutākhkhirūn) reviewed earlier transmitted rulings and each 'corrected' (ṣaḥḥaḥa) a position. The final preference is determined by further authorities like al-Baḥr and al-Hidāya, establishing the school's relied-upon view.
This is a classic example of tarjīḥ among variant transmissions (riwāyāt).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقصار: اعلم أن القصار إما أن يكون عمله في الثوب إحداث لون كالصبغ أو القصر بالنشا، أو ببياض البيض، ففيه له حق الحبس اتفاقا أو يكون أثر عمله إزالة الدرن وإظهار البياض المستتر، فقد اختلف التصحيح فيه، فإنه ذكر قاضي خان في "شرحه"، وصححه أن له حق الحبس في هذه الصورة أيضا؛ لأن البياض كان مستترا وقد ظهر بفعله، فكأنه أحدثه فيه ويؤيده إطلاق المصنف أيضا، وصحح المصنف في "مستصفاه" معزيا إلى "الذخيرة" أن ليس له حق الحبس، قال في "البحر" فاختلف التصحيح، وينبغي ترجيح المنع، وقد جزم به صاحب "الهداية".
And the fuller: Know that the fuller's work in the garment is either producing a color like dyeing or sizing with starch or egg white, so he has the right of retention by agreement, or his work's effect is removing dirt and revealing hidden whiteness. Then the tashīh has differed on this. Qādhī Khān in his Sharh corrected that he has the right of retention in this case too, because the whiteness was hidden and appeared by his action, so it is as if he produced it; the absolute statement of the author supports this. The author in his Mustasfa corrected, attributing to al-Dhakhīra, that he does not have the right of retention. Al-Bahr said: the tashīh differs, and the preferred view is to reject (the right), and the author of al-Hidāya affirmed it.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific application of the retention rule to the fuller (one who cleans and whitens garments). It distinguishes two types of fuller work: (1) adding color or sizing, which clearly creates an effect (agreed right of retention); (2) removing dirt to reveal hidden whiteness. For the latter, there is a dispute among later authorities. Qādī Khān corrected that it still counts as creating an effect because the whiteness did not exist visibly before. However, the author of Kanz al-Daqā'iq (al-Nasafī) in his Mustasfa, citing al-Dhakhīra, corrected that it does not give the right of retention. Al-Bahr notes the conflict of tashīh (the preferred correction) and recommends siding with denial, which al-Hidāya also affirmed. This shows the internal Hanafi process of tarjīh among later scholars.

Key Terms
القصار (al-qaṣṣār): The fuller, a craftsman who cleans and whitens cloth.
التصحيح (al-tashīḥ): The act of correcting or preferring a ruling among variant transmissions within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (tarjīḥ), does a fuller who only removes dirt have the right to detain the garment for his wage?
A) Yes, because the dirt removal is an effect.
B) No, because the whiteness was already present.
C) Yes, by consensus.
D) No, because the work does not create a new attribute.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a craftsman's right to detain requires the creation of a new attribute; merely revealing an inherent quality does not suffice.

Liability and Wage After Detention: Imam vs. Two Disciples
Ruling on loss after detention: Imam vs. two disciples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding liability and wage when a hired craftsman detains the object and it is lost.

Core Idea
Detention without transgression does not create liability according to Imam, but the two disciples hold the object already guaranteed.

When a hired craftsman detains the object as security for his wage and it is accidentally lost, does he bear liability and is he entitled to his wage? This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute on this question, presenting the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Imam's view)
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: no liability and no wage. Understand his reasoning that the detention was not transgressive, so the object remains a trust.
Imam's view is based on the absence of transgression (ghayr mutaʿaddī).
2
Identify the opponents and their view
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the object was already guaranteed before detention, so it remains guarantee after; the owner has an option between two forms of compensation.
The two disciples consider the hire contract itself as creating a guarantee.
3
Follow the opponents' proof
Understand the basis of the two disciples: the object was in the hirer's guarantee due to the hire contract; detention does not change its status.
They focus on the contractual relationship rather than the act of detention.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Note that the passage does not provide a rebuttal from Imam; it simply presents both positions. This is a pure exposition of ikhtilaf.
The absence of a response indicates the dispute is acknowledged but not resolved here.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under Imam's view, the craftsman is not liable but loses his wage; under the two disciples' view, the owner can choose to recover the value without paying wage or pay wage and recover the full value.
The choice affects compensation and wage entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا ضمان: هذا عند الإمام؛ لأنه غير متعد في الحبس، فبقي أمانة كما كان عنده، ولا أجر له؛ لهلاك المعقود عليه قبل التسليم وعندهما العين كانت مضمونة قبل الحبس، فكذا بعده، لكنه بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه غير معمول ولا أجر له وإن شاء معمولا وله الأجر
So no guarantee: this according to the Imam, because he is not transgressing in the detention, so it remains a trust as it was with him, and he has no wage due to destruction of the contracted object before delivery. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the object was already liable before detention, so likewise after, but he has the option: if he wishes, he may make him liable for the unworked object and he has no wage; if he wishes, for the worked object and he has the wage.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage explains the consequence when the hired person detains the object and it is lost. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. According to Abu Hanifa, since the detention was not transgressive (he had the right to detain), the object remains a trust in his hands; thus he is not liable for its loss, but he forfeits his wage because the contracted object (the work) was destroyed before delivery. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the object was already under guarantee (for the hire) even before detention, so detention does not change that; however, the owner has an option: either to claim compensation for the value of the object without the work and pay no wage, or to claim compensation for the value with the work and pay the full wage. This dispute affects practical cases where a craftsman detains and the item is accidentally destroyed.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Legal liability for loss or damage.
غير متعد (ghayr mutaʿaddī): Not transgressing; acting within one's legal right.
أمانة (amānah): Trust; an object held without liability for accidental loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is liable for the value and forfeits the wage.
B) He is not liable but forfeits the wage.
C) He is liable but can claim the wage.
D) He is neither liable nor loses the wage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if a hired person detains without transgression, Imam Abu Hanifa exempts from liability but forfeits the wage, while the two disciples impose liability with owner's option.

No Right to Detain for Those Without Effect
Ruling on detention for workers with no effect, with intra-Hanafi dispute on definition of 'effect'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on detention for workers without effect and distinguish between the two definitions of 'effect' (athar) by their practical consequences.

Core Idea
A hired worker whose work leaves no lasting effect on the object has no right to detain it; wrongful detention makes him a usurper.

The right to detain an object for unpaid wages depends on whether the worker's labor leaves a discernible 'effect' on the object. But what exactly counts as an 'effect'? This lesson unpacks a classic Hanafi dispute over the definition of athar and its impact on the right of retention, using examples from daily hire like porters, dyers, and woodcutters.

Guided Path
1
Identify workers without effect
Note the examples given: porter (hammaal) and sailor (mallaah). Their work is pure service; it does not alter the object in a lasting way.
The contracted work is the action itself, not a quality in the object.
2
Understand the legal consequence of wrongful detention
If such a worker detains the object, he becomes a usurper (ghaasib) and is liable for full compensation. The owner can choose to value the object as worked (and pay wage) or as unworked (and pay no wage).
This option highlights the equitable balance in Hanafi law.
3
Grasp the two definitions of 'effect'
First view: effect must be a foreign substance attached to the object (e.g., starch, dye). Second view: effect is any visible change (e.g., splitting wood, grinding, shaving a head).
The first view is narrower; the second is broader.
4
Trace the author's preference
The author leans to the first definition because the contracted object is described as a 'quality in the garment', implying a connected additive. He also notes that Al-Qunyah preferred the second view, but the reasoning points to the first.
This is an intra-Hanafi tarjih (preference).
5
Apply the preferred view to a new case
Test with a woodcutter: under the first view, no detention right; under the second, detention right exists. This shows the practical difference.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the first view: connected substance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لا أثر لعمله كالحمال والملاح على الصانع: لأن المعقود عليه نفس العمل، وهو غير قائم في العين، فلا يتصور حبسه، فليس له ولاية الحبس، فعلم أنه لو حبسها ضمنها ضمان الغاصب، وصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمتها محمولة، وله الأجر، وإن شاء غير محمولة، فلا أجر له كذا في "الجوهرة"، واختلفوا في المراد من الأثر، فقيل أن تكون الأثر متصلة بمحل العمل كالنشا والصبغ، وقيل: أن يرى ويعاين في محل العمل، وثمرته تظهر في كسر الحطب وطحن الحنطة، وحلق رأس العبد، فمن أراد بالأثر اتصاله بمحل العمل فليس للصانع حق الحبس عنده، ومن أراد المعنى الثاني، فعنده له الحبس في هذه الصورة أيضا، وظاهر ما في "القنية" ترجيح الثاني، والذي يظهر من كلامهم ترجيح الأول؛ لما عللوا به في حق الحبس من أن المعقود عليه وصف في الثوب. وكذا قولهم: كالحمال: قد ضبطه بعضهم بالجيم المعجمة والأولى أن يكون بالحاء؛ لأن الحمل يجوز أن يقع على الظهر والدابة فيكون أعم.
And those whose work has no effect, like the porter and the sailor from the craftsman? Because the contracted object is the work itself, and it does not subsist in the object, so its detention cannot be conceived, so he has no authority of detention. So it is known that if he detains it, he guarantees it as a usurper's guarantee, and its owner has the option: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value carried, and he has the wage; if he wishes, unloaded, and he has no wage. Thus in Al-Jawhara. And they differed on the meaning of 'effect'. It was said that the effect must be connected to the workplace like starch and dye. It was said: that it is seen and observed in the workplace, and its fruit appears in breaking wood, grinding wheat, and shaving the head of a slave. So whoever intends by 'effect' its connection to the workplace, then the craftsman has no right of retention according to him; and whoever intends the second meaning, then according to him he has retention in this case too. The apparent in Al-Qunyah is a preference for the second. What appears from their words is preference for the first, because of their reasoning on the right of retention that the contracted object is a quality in the garment. And similarly their statement: like the porter: some wrote it with jim and it is more appropriate to be with ha, because carrying may occur on the back or beast, so it is more general.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the right to detain, now focusing on hired persons whose work does not leave an effect on the object, such as porters (who transport goods) and sailors (who navigate boats). For these, the contracted work is the action itself, not a quality in the object, so there is no basis for detention. If they nonetheless detain, they become liable as usurpers (ḍāmin al-ghāṣib), and the owner has an option: either to demand compensation for the object as it was before the work (unworked) and pay no wage, or to demand compensation for the worked object and pay the full wage. Then the passage explores the definition of 'effect' (athar) which determines the right to detain. Two definitions are given: (1) the effect must be a foreign substance attached to the object (like starch or dye); (2) the effect must be a visible change in the object (like broken wood, ground flour, shaved head). The first definition excludes cases like woodcutting or grinding, while the second includes them. The commentary notes that Al-Qunyah prefers the second, but the author's own analysis leans to the first, based on the earlier reasoning that the contracted object is a quality subsisting in the garment. Finally, a linguistic note: the word 'ḥammāl' (porter) is correctly spelled with ḥā, not jīm, to encompass carrying on back or animal.

Key Terms
الأثر (al-athar): The effect of the hired work on the object; its presence gives the right to detain.
ضمان الغاصب (ḍamān al-ghāṣib): The liability of a usurper, which includes compensation for the full value.
الحمال (al-ḥammāl): A porter, a worker who carries goods.
الملاح (al-mallāḥ): A sailor, a worker who navigates a boat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, which of the following craftsmen would have the right to detain the object for his wage?
A) A laborer who grinds flour.
B) A porter who carries goods.
C) A dyer who dyes cloth.
D) A woodcutter who splits logs.

Key Takeaway
A hired worker's right to detain depends on whether his work leaves a lasting effect on the object; the preferred Hanafi view requires that effect to be a connected foreign substance.

Exception for Returning a Runaway Slave: Right to Detain for Reward
Exception to the rule that those without effect cannot detain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exception that a person who returns a runaway slave may detain him for the reward, and explain the rationale based on the analogy to a sale.

Core Idea
Saving a runaway slave from loss gives the finder a right to detain him for reward, like a seller detains goods.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a hired person whose work leaves no effect on the object cannot detain the object for his wage. However, Hanafi law recognizes an exception: the person who returns a runaway slave (al-ābiq) to its owner may detain the slave until his reward is paid. This exception is based on the idea that the slave was on the verge of being lost, and the finder revived him. The passage draws an analogy to a sale: as if the finder sold the slave back to the owner, so he gains the right of detention. This lesson will unpack this exception and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Recall the general rule
State the rule from the previous lesson: a hired person whose work has no effect on the object cannot detain the object for his wage.
The general rule is based on the absence of any trace of work in the object.
2
Identify the exception
Note that returning a runaway slave (رد الآبق) is an exception: the returner can detain the slave for the reward, even though his act of returning leaves no physical effect on the slave.
The exception is explicitly stated in the text: 'واستثنى من هذه القاعدة رد الآبق'.
3
Understand the rationale
The text provides the illa: the slave was on the verge of destruction (كان على شرف الهلاك) and the returner revived him by returning (أحياه بالرد). This is like saving property from loss.
The concept of 'revival' (إحياء) is key – the finder's action prevented total loss.
4
Apply the analogy to sale
The text says 'كأنه باعه منه' (as if he sold him to him). In a sale, the seller has the right to detain the goods until payment. By analogy, the returner may detain the slave until the reward is paid.
This analogy (qiyas) establishes a legal right that is not present in ordinary hire contracts.
5
Note the scope
This exception is specific to returning a runaway slave. It does not extend to other services without effect; the illa is the risk of loss and the action of saving.
If the object is not in danger of destruction, the exception does not apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يحبس للأجر واستثنى من هذه القاعدة رد الآبق فإن للراد حق حبس العبد الآبق لاستيفاء الأجر وإن لم يكن لعمله أثر في العين؛ لأنه كان على شرف الهلاك، وقد أحياه بالرد، فكأنه باعه منه فله حق الحبس
He does not detain for the wage. And an exception from this rule is the returning of a runaway slave, for the returner has the right to detain the runaway slave to receive the reward, even though his work has no effect in the object; because he was on the verge of destruction, and he revived him by returning, so it is as if he sold him to him, so he has the right of detention.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage states an exception to the general rule that a hired person whose work has no effect cannot detain the object for his wage. The exception is for the person who returns a runaway slave (ābiq). The finder is entitled to a reward for his action, and he may detain the slave until that reward is paid. The reason given is that the slave was on the verge of being lost or destroyed, and the finder effectively saved him, which is analogous to a sale: as if the finder 'sold' the slave back to the owner. Thus, he gains the right of detention by analogy to a seller. This shows that the right of detention is not limited to craftsmen with physical effects; it can arise from a beneficial action that saves property from loss.

Key Terms
رد الآبق (radd al-ābiq): Returning a runaway slave to his owner.
حق الحبس (haqq al-habs): Right of detention – the legal right to retain an object until a claim (here, the reward) is satisfied.
أجر (ajr): Reward or compensation paid for a beneficial act, such as returning a runaway slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the person who returns a runaway slave have the right to detain him for the reward, even though his work leaves no effect?
A) Because the reward is considered a wage for labor.
B) Because the slave was about to be lost, and returning him is like a sale.
C) Because the finder's work leaves a legal effect in the slave.
D) Because the finder is considered a hired worker.

Key Takeaway
The returner of a runaway slave may detain the slave for reward because the act of saving the slave from loss is analogized to a sale, granting a right of detention even without physical effect.

Subcontracting in Ijara: Personal Service vs. Absolute
Ruling on subcontracting in Ijara based on condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a contract with a stipulation of personal service and an absolute contract in Ijara, and state the Hanafi ruling on subcontracting for each.

Core Idea
Personal service stipulation bars delegation; absolute hire allows subcontracting.

This lesson examines a common situation in hiring contracts: can the hired person hire someone else to do the work? The answer depends on the wording of the contract. We will learn the Hanafi ruling based on whether personal service is stipulated or the contract is absolute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Determine if the contract includes a clear stipulation that the work must be done personally (e.g., 'work with yourself, not with another's hand') or if it is unconditional (absolute, like 'that you work').
The Arabic phrasing used in the contract is decisive.
2
Apply the ruling based on type
If personal service is stipulated, the hired person cannot subcontract; if he does, he forfeits the wage. If the contract is absolute, he may delegate to another.
The wage is only earned if the contract terms are respected.
3
Note the exception for the wet-nurse
The wet-nurse (ẓi'r) is an exception—she may hire another to nurse even if personal service was stipulated, because her personal presence is not indispensable for the child's benefit.
This exception is recorded in Al-Khulāṣa.
4
Understand the rationale
In an absolute contract, the obligation is a work in the hired person's liability (dhimmah), which can be fulfilled either personally or by proxy, similar to repaying a debt.
This reasoning is cited from Al-Fatḥ and Al-Baḥr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن شرط عمله بنفسه: صورة المسألة: أن رجلا استأجر رجلا آخر على عمل وشرط عليه أن يعمله بنفسه بأن قال له : اعمل بنفسك، ولا تعمل بيد غيرك، فليس للأجير أن يستعمل على عمله آخر؛ لأن المعقود عليه العمل من محل معين فلا يقوم غيره مقامه، فإذا استعمل غيره لا يستحق الأجر، واستثنى في "الخلاصة" الظئر، فإن لها أن تستعمل غيرها، وهذا إذا قال: اعمل بنفسك ولا تعمل بيد غيرك وأما إذا قال على أن تعمل، فهو من قبيل الإطلاق، وله أن يستعمل غيره. كذا في الفتح والبحر مع توضيح. وإن أطلق لأن الواجب عليه عمل في ذمته، ويمكنه الإيفاء بنفسه والاستيفاء بغيره كالمأمور بقضاء الدين
If he stipulates his own work: the form of the issue is that a man hires another man for work and stipulates that he do it himself, saying: 'Work with yourself and do not work with another's hand.' Then the hired person may not employ another for his work, because the contracted work is from a specific person, so no one else can stand in his place. If he employs another, he does not deserve the wage. An exception is made in al-Khulāṣa for the wet-nurse, for she may employ another. This is if he says: 'Work yourself and do not work with another's hand.' But if he says: 'That you work,' it is of the type of absolute (without condition), and he may employ another. Thus in al-Fatḥ and al-Baḥr with clarification. And if he is absolute, because the obligation upon him is work in his liability; he can fulfill it himself or have it fulfilled by another, like the one ordered to repay a debt.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage addresses whether a hired person can hire someone else to do the work. If the contract explicitly stipulates that he must do the work himself (e.g., 'work with yourself and do not use another's hand'), then he cannot subcontract; if he does, he forfeits the wage. An exception is the wet-nurse (ẓi'r), who may employ a substitute even if stipulated because her personal service is not essential for the child's benefit. If the contract is not explicit (absolute), the hired person may hire another because the obligation is on his liability: he can fulfill it either personally or through a delegate, similar to paying a debt. This is based on the principle that the work is a liability (mā fī dhimmah) which can be discharged by proxy.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-sharṭ): A stipulation in the contract that the work be done personally.
الإطلاق (al-iṭlāq): An unconditional contract without specification of personal service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) If the contract is absolute and does not require personal service.
C) If the hirer agreed later.
D) Never, because the work is personal.

Key Takeaway
The hired person's ability to subcontract depends on whether the contract stipulates personal service or is absolute.

Hiring to Bring Family: Proportional Wage
Ruling on proportional wage in hire of transport when some family die.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportional wage due in a hire contract when some family members die during transport, and identify the conditions under which the contract becomes void requiring ujrat al-mithl.

Core Idea
Wage is proportional to actual transport of persons, not distance; unknown members void the contract.

When you hire someone to bring your family, what happens if some die before the return trip? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on proportional wages, the underlying rationale, and important qualifications from later scholars that refine the basic rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and basic ruling
The act: hiring a person to bring family members. The basic ruling: if some die, the hired person gets a proportional wage.
The wage is not forfeited entirely.
2
Understand the rationale
Wage is compensation for transporting persons, not for distance. Thus, partial performance earns proportional wage.
Full wage for the outward trip (completed), reduced wage for return (only survivors).
3
Note the two qualifications from Abu Jaʿfar
First: if the burden (mu'na) of the deceased equals that of survivors (e.g., all adults), no reduction; full wage due. Second: the ruling applies only if family members were known (specified) in the contract.
These qualifications are recorded by later Hanafi commentators.
4
Recognize the internal dispute on unknown family
Abu Jaʿfar holds that proportional wage is due even if unknown; al-Qahistānī says the contract is void (fasid) requiring the equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl).
The later preferred view is al-Qahistānī's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استأجره ليجيء بعياله ومات بعضهم، فجاء من بقي، فله أجره بحسابه: لأنه أو فى بعض المعقود عليه، فيستحق الأجر بقدره، ومعنى قوله: "فله أجره بحسابه" أي فله أجر الذهاب بكماله وأجر المجيء بقدر من بقي؛ لأن الأجر مقابل بنقل العيال لا بقطع المسافة، وقد قيد الفقيه أبو جعفر الله هذه المسألة بقيدين: أحدهما: ما نقله الشارح ملا مسكين أن هذا إذا قلت مؤونة البعض عن مؤونة الكل، أما لو استوت مؤونتهما بأن مات الكبار مثلا، فله الأجر كله وثانيهما ما نقله الزيلعي: أن المسألة مقيدة بما إذا كانوا معلومين حتى يكون الأجر مقابلا بجميعهم، فإذا مات البعض انتقص أجر الميت من أجر الكل، وأما إذا لم يكونوا معلومين، فلا يكون الأجر مقابلا بجملتهم، لكن ما ذكره الفقيه أبي جعفر محله من وجوب الأجر إذا كانوا غير معلومين مخالف لما في "القهستاني" حيث قال: فإن جهلوا فسدت الإجارة، ووجب أجر المثل. (ملخص ما في البحر والفتح)
And if he hired him to come with his family and some of them died, and he came with the remaining, then he has his wage proportionally: because he fulfilled part of the contracted, so he deserves the wage to that extent. The meaning of his statement 'so he has his wage proportionally' is that he has the full wage for the journey there and the wage for the journey back proportionally to those remaining, because the wage is in exchange for transporting the family, not for traversing distance. The jurist Abu Jaʿfar (may God...) qualified this issue with two restrictions: one: what the commentator Mulla Miskin narrated, that this is when the burden of the few (dead) is less than the burden of the whole; but if their burden is equal, for example if the adults died, then he has the full wage. The second: what al-Zaylaʿī narrated, that the issue is restricted to when they were known (specified) so that the wage is in exchange for all of them; if some die, the wage of the deceased is deducted from the total. But if they are not known, then the wage is not in exchange for the whole. However, what Abu Jaʿfar mentioned about the obligation of the wage when they are unknown contradicts what is in al-Qahistānī, where he said: if they are unknown, the lease is void and the equivalent wage is obligatory. (Summary from al-Baḥr and al-Fatḥ)
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a person hires someone to go to Basra and bring his family members back. If some family members die before the journey back, the hired person is entitled to a proportional wage: full wage for the outward trip (since that is completed) and a reduced wage for the return trip based on the number of family members he actually brings. The wage is considered compensation for transporting people, not for distance traveled. The passage then records two qualifications from later scholars: (1) If the deceased family members were easier to transport (e.g., children) than those who survived, the reduction is proportional; if they were equally burdensome (e.g., adults), no reduction. (2) This calculation applies only if the family members were individually identified in the contract; if they were unknown, the contract may be void (fasid) requiring an equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl), contrary to Abu Jafar's position that the wage would still be owed proportionally. This reflects the internal Hanafi process of qualifying general rulings with conditions.

Key Terms
أجر مثله (ujrat mithlihi): The equivalent wage, determined by market rates, due when a lease is void.
مؤونة (mu'na): Burden or expense of transporting a person; used in the qualification to determine proportional reduction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hired person was to bring a family of five, but two children die before the return trip, according to the basic rule, how much wage does he get?
A) Full wage for outward trip and reduced wage for return trip proportionally.
B) No wage at all because the contract is broken.
C) Only the wage for the return trip.
D) Full wage for both trips.

Key Takeaway
In hire contracts for transporting persons, wage is proportional to the actual number transported; unknown persons void the contract and trigger ujrat al-mithl.
